Title: National Security Act 2023
Date: 2024-10-23
Publisher: Statute Law Database
Identifier: http://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2023/32

## National Security Act 2023

                                                   B e it enacted  by the
King’s most Excellent Majesty, by and with the advice and consent of the Lords
Spiritual and Temporal, and Commons, in this present Parliament assembled, and
by the authority of the same, as follows:—

### Espionage, sabotage and persons acting for foreign powers

#### Espionage etc

##### Obtaining or disclosing protected information

1

1.1

A person commits an offence if—

1.1.a

the person—

1.1.a.i

obtains, copies, records or retains protected information, or

1.1.a.ii

discloses or provides access to protected information,

1.1.b

the person’s conduct is for a purpose that they know, or having regard to
other matters known to them ought reasonably to know, is prejudicial to the
safety or interests of the United Kingdom, and

1.1.c

the foreign power condition is met in relation to the person’s conduct (see
section  31 ).

1.2

In  this section  “ protected information ” means any information, document or
other article where, for the purpose of protecting the safety or interests of
the United Kingdom—

1.2.a

access to the information, document or other article is restricted in any way,
or

1.2.b

it is reasonable to expect that access to the information, document or other
article would be restricted in any way.

1.3

Subsection (1)  applies whether the person’s conduct takes place in the United
Kingdom or elsewhere.

1.4

A person who commits an offence under  this section  is liable on conviction
on indictment to imprisonment for life or a fine (or both).

1.5

For the purposes of  this section —

1.5.a

a person retains protected information if the person retains it in their
possession or under their control;

1.5.b

disclosure includes parting with possession.

##### Obtaining or disclosing trade secrets

2

2.1

A person commits an offence if—

2.1.a

the person—

2.1.a.i

obtains, copies, records or retains a trade secret, or

2.1.a.ii

discloses or provides access to a trade secret,

2.1.b

the person’s conduct is unauthorised,

2.1.c

the person knows, or having regard to other matters known to them ought
reasonably to know, that their conduct is unauthorised, and

2.1.d

the foreign power condition is met in relation to the person’s conduct (see
section  31 ).

2.2

A “ trade secret ” means any information, document or other article which—

2.2.a

is not generally known by, or available to, persons with knowledge of or
expertise in the field to which it relates,

2.2.b

has actual or potential industrial, economic or commercial value which would
be, or could reasonably be expected to be, adversely affected if it became
generally known by, or available to, such persons, and

2.2.c

could reasonably be expected to be subject to measures to prevent it becoming
generally known by, or available to, such persons (whether or not it is
actually subject to such measures).

2.3

A person’s conduct is unauthorised if the person—

2.3.a

is not entitled to determine whether they may engage in the conduct, and

2.3.b

does not have consent to engage in the conduct from a person who is so
entitled.

2.4

Subsection  (1)  applies whether the person’s conduct takes place in the
United Kingdom or elsewhere (but see  subsection (5) ).

2.5

Conduct within subsection  (1)  which takes place wholly outside the United
Kingdom constitutes an offence only if the trade secret is in the possession
or under the control of a UK person.

2.6

A “ UK person ” means—

2.6.a

a United Kingdom national;

2.6.b

an individual who lives in the United Kingdom;

2.6.c

a body incorporated under the law of a part of the United Kingdom;

2.6.d

an unincorporated association formed under the law of a part of the United
Kingdom.

2.7

A “United Kingdom national” is an individual who is—

2.7.a

a British citizen, a British overseas territories citizen, a British National
(Overseas) or a British Overseas citizen,

2.7.b

a person who under the British Nationality Act 1981 is a British subject, or

2.7.c

a British protected person within the meaning of that Act.

2.8

A person who commits an offence under this section is liable on conviction on
indictment to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 14 years or a fine (or
both).

2.9

For the purposes of  this section —

2.9.a

a person retains a trade secret if they retain it in their possession or under
their control;

2.9.b

disclosure includes parting with possession.

##### Assisting a foreign intelligence service

3

3.1

A person commits an offence if the person—

3.1.a

engages in conduct of any kind, and

3.1.b

intends that conduct to materially assist a foreign intelligence service in
carrying out UK-related activities.

3.2

A person commits an offence if the person—

3.2.a

engages in conduct that is likely to materially assist a foreign intelligence
service in carrying out UK-related activities, and

3.2.b

knows, or having regard to other matters known to them ought reasonably to
know, that their conduct is likely to materially assist a foreign intelligence
service in carrying out UK-related activities.

3.3

Conduct that may be likely to materially assist a foreign intelligence service
includes providing, or providing access to, information, goods, services or
financial benefits (whether directly or indirectly).

3.4

“ UK-related activities ” means—

3.4.a

activities taking place in the United Kingdom;

3.4.b

activities taking place outside the United Kingdom which are prejudicial to
the safety or interests of the United Kingdom.

3.5

For the purposes of  subsections (1)  and  (2)  it is not necessary to
identify a particular foreign intelligence service.

3.6

Subsections (1)  and  (2)  apply to conduct outside the United Kingdom, but
apply to conduct taking place wholly outside the United Kingdom only if the
person engaging in the conduct—

3.6.a

is a UK person, or

3.6.b

acts for or on behalf of, or holds office under, the Crown, or is in Crown
employment (whether or not they engage in the conduct in that capacity).

3.7

In proceedings for an offence under this section it is a defence to show that
the person engaged in the conduct in question—

3.7.a

in compliance with a legal obligation under the law of the United Kingdom
which is not a legal obligation under private law,

3.7.b

in the case of a person having functions of a public nature under the law of
the United Kingdom, for the purposes of those functions,

3.7.c

as a lawyer carrying on a legal activity, or

3.7.d

in accordance with, or in relation to UK-related activities carried out in
accordance with, an agreement or arrangement to which—

3.7.d.i

the United Kingdom was a party, or

3.7.d.ii

any person acting for or on behalf of, or holding office under, the Crown was
(in that capacity) a party.

3.8

A person is taken to have shown a matter mentioned in subsection  (7)  if—

3.8.a

sufficient evidence of the matter is adduced to raise an issue with respect to
it, and

3.8.b

the contrary is not proved beyond reasonable doubt.

3.9

A person who commits an offence under  this section  is liable on conviction
on indictment to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 14 years or a fine (or
both).

3.10

In  this section —

                                    “ Crown employment ” means employment
under or for the purposes of a government department or any officer or body
exercising on behalf of the Crown functions conferred by an enactment;
“ financial benefit ” means money or money’s worth;
“ foreign intelligence service ” means any person whose functions include
carrying out intelligence activities for or on behalf of a foreign power;
the “ law of the United Kingdom ” includes the law of any part of the United
Kingdom;
“ lawyer ” has the meaning given by paragraph  6 (3)  of Schedule  15 ;
“ legal activity ” has the meaning given by paragraph  6 (4)  of Schedule  15
;
“ UK person ” has the same meaning as in section  2 .

#### Entering and inspecting places used for defence etc

##### Entering etc a prohibited place for a purpose prejudicial to the UK

4

4.1

A person commits an offence if—

4.1.a

the person—

4.1.a.i

accesses, enters, inspects, passes over or under, approaches or is in the
vicinity of a prohibited place, or

4.1.a.ii

causes an unmanned vehicle or device to access, enter, inspect, pass over or
under, approach or be in the vicinity of a prohibited place, and

4.1.b

that conduct is for a purpose that the person knows, or having regard to other
matters known to them ought reasonably to know, is prejudicial to the safety
or interests of the United Kingdom.

4.2

In  subsection (1) (a)  a reference to inspecting a prohibited place includes—

4.2.a

taking, or procuring the taking of, photographs, videos or other recordings of
the prohibited place;

4.2.b

inspecting photographs, videos or other recordings of the prohibited place.

4.3

For the purposes of  this section , a person engages in conduct mentioned in
subsection (1) (a)  if the person does so in person or by electronic or remote
means.

4.4

Subsection  (1)  applies whether the person’s conduct takes place in the
United Kingdom or elsewhere.

4.5

A person who commits an offence under  this section  is liable on conviction
on indictment to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 14 years or a fine (or
both).

4.6

In this Part “ vehicle ” means any form of transport.

##### Unauthorised entry etc to a prohibited place

5

5.1

A person commits an offence if—

5.1.a

the person—

5.1.a.i

accesses, enters, inspects or passes over or under a prohibited place, or

5.1.a.ii

causes an unmanned vehicle or device to access, enter, inspect or pass over or
under a prohibited place,

5.1.b

that conduct is unauthorised, and

5.1.c

the person knows, or having regard to other matters known to them ought
reasonably to know, that their conduct is unauthorised.

5.2

A person’s conduct is unauthorised if the person—

5.2.a

is not entitled to determine whether they may engage in the conduct, and

5.2.b

does not have consent to engage in the conduct from a person so entitled.

5.3

In  subsection (1) (a)  a reference to inspecting a prohibited place includes
taking, or procuring the taking of, photographs, videos or other recordings of
the prohibited place.

5.4

For the purposes of  this section , a person engages in conduct mentioned in
subsection (1) (a)  if the person does so in person or by electronic or remote
means.

5.5

A person who commits an offence under  this section  is liable—

5.5.a

on summary conviction in England and Wales, to imprisonment for a term not
exceeding the maximum term for summary offences or a fine (or both);

5.5.b

on summary conviction in Scotland, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 6
months or a fine not exceeding level 5 on the standard scale (or both);

5.5.c

on summary conviction in Northern Ireland, to imprisonment for a term not
exceeding 6 months or a fine not exceeding level 5 on the standard scale (or
both).

##### Powers of police officers in relation to a prohibited place

6

6.1

A constable may order—

6.1.a

a person not to engage, or to cease to engage, in conduct mentioned in
section 4 (1) (a)  (whether in person or by electronic or remote means) in
relation to a prohibited place;

6.1.b

a person who has accessed or entered a prohibited place (whether in person or
by electronic or remote means) to leave it immediately;

6.1.c

a person in an area adjacent to a prohibited place to leave the area
immediately;

6.1.d

the driver or person in charge of a vehicle or device (whether in person or by
electronic or remote means) in a prohibited place, or in an area adjacent to a
prohibited place, to move the vehicle or device from the place or area
immediately.

6.2

A constable may arrange for—

6.2.a

the removal of a vehicle or device from a prohibited place or an area adjacent
to a prohibited place;

6.2.b

the movement of a vehicle or device within a prohibited place or an area
adjacent to a prohibited place.

6.3

A constable may not exercise a power under  subsection (1)  or  (2)  unless
the constable reasonably believes that exercising the power is necessary to
protect the safety or interests of the United Kingdom.

6.4

A person commits an offence if the person fails to comply with an order
imposed under  subsection (1) .

6.5

A person who commits an offence under  this section  is liable on summary
conviction to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 3 months or a fine not
exceeding level 4 on the standard scale (or both).

##### Meaning of “prohibited place”

7

7.1

In this Part “ prohibited place ” means—

7.1.a

Crown land in the United Kingdom or the Sovereign Base Areas of Akrotiri and
Dhekelia which is used—

7.1.a.i

for UK defence purposes;

7.1.a.ii

for extracting any metals, oil or minerals for use for UK defence purposes;

7.1.a.iii

for the purposes of the defence of a foreign country or territory;

7.1.b

a vehicle—

7.1.b.i

situated in the United Kingdom or the Sovereign Base Areas of Akrotiri and
Dhekelia which is used for UK defence purposes or for the purposes of the
defence of a foreign country or territory;

7.1.b.ii

not so situated which is used for UK defence purposes;

7.1.c

any land or building in the United Kingdom or the Sovereign Base Areas of
Akrotiri and Dhekelia which is used for the purposes described in  subsection
(2) (b)  or  (3) (b)  (or both);

7.1.d

any land or building in the United Kingdom or the Sovereign Base Areas of
Akrotiri and Dhekelia which is—

7.1.d.i

owned or controlled by the Security Service, the Secret Intelligence Service
or GCHQ, and

7.1.d.ii

used for the functions of the Security Service, the Secret Intelligence
Service or GCHQ;

7.1.e

any land or building or vehicle designated as a prohibited place in
regulations made under  section 8 .

7.2

In  subsection (1)  use for UK defence purposes means use for the purposes of—

7.2.a

the activities of the armed forces of the Crown,

7.2.b

the invention, development, production, operation, storage or disposal of
weapons or other equipment or capabilities of those forces and research
relating to it,

7.2.c

United Kingdom defence policy and strategy and military planning and
intelligence, or

7.2.d

plans and measures for the maintenance of essential supplies and services that
are or would be needed by the United Kingdom in time of war.

7.3

In  subsection (1)  use for the purposes of the defence of a foreign country
or territory means use for the purposes of—

7.3.a

the activities of the armed forces of the foreign country or territory, or

7.3.b

the invention, development, production, operation, storage or disposal of
weapons or other equipment or capabilities of those forces and research
relating to it.

7.4

In  this section —

                                    “ building ” includes any part of a
building;
“ Crown land ” means any land or building in which there is a Crown interest
or a Duchy interest;
“ Crown interest ” means any of the following—
an interest belonging to His Majesty in right of the Crown or in right of His
private estates;
an interest belonging to a United Kingdom government department or held in
trust for His Majesty for the purposes of a United Kingdom government
department;
“ Duchy interest ” means an interest belonging to His Majesty in right of the
Duchy of Lancaster or belonging to the Duchy of Cornwall;
“ foreign country or territory ” means a country or territory outside the
United Kingdom, the Channel Islands, the Isle of Man or the British Overseas
Territories;
“ GCHQ ” has the meaning given by section 3(3) of the Intelligence Services
Act 1994.

7.5

In  subsection (4)  the reference to His Majesty’s private estates is to be
construed in accordance with section 1 of the Crown Private Estates Act 1862.

##### Power to designate additional sites as prohibited places

8

8.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations designate—

8.1.a

land or a building situated in the United Kingdom or the Sovereign Base Areas
of Akrotiri and Dhekelia, or

8.1.b

a vehicle,

as a prohibited place.

8.2

The power in  subsection (1)  may be exercised only if, having regard to the
matters mentioned in  subsection (3) , the Secretary of State reasonably
considers it necessary to do so in order to protect the safety or interests of
the United Kingdom.

8.3

Those matters are—

8.3.a

the purpose for which the land or building or vehicle is used;

8.3.b

the nature of any information held, stored or processed on the land or in the
building or vehicle;

8.3.c

the nature of any technology, equipment or material located on the land or in
the building or vehicle.

8.4

The power in  subsection (1)  may be exercised in relation to—

8.4.a

a description of land or buildings, or

8.4.b

a description of vehicle,

as well as in relation to particular land or buildings or a particular
vehicle.

8.5

In  this section  “ building ” includes any part of a building.

##### Power to designate a cordoned area to secure defence aircraft

9

9.1

A constable may designate an area as a cordoned area.

9.2

A constable may designate an area under  subsection (1)  only if the constable
considers it expedient to do so for the purposes of securing—

9.2.a

an aircraft, or a part of an aircraft, used for military purposes, or

9.2.b

equipment relating to such an aircraft.

9.3

If a designation is made orally, the constable making the designation must
confirm it in writing as soon as is reasonably practicable.

9.4

A constable making a designation must, as soon as is reasonably practicable—

9.4.a

make a written record of the time at which the designation was made, and

9.4.b

ensure that a police officer of at least the rank of superintendent is
informed.

9.5

An officer who is informed of a designation in accordance with  subsection (4)
(b)  must—

9.5.a

confirm the designation or cancel it with effect from such time as the officer
may direct, and

9.5.b

if the officer cancels the designation, make a written record of the
cancellation and the reason for it.

9.6

A constable making a designation must arrange for the demarcation of the
cordoned area, so far as is reasonably practicable—

9.6.a

by means of tape marked with the word “police”, or

9.6.b

in such other manner as the constable considers appropriate.

##### Duration of cordon

10

10.1

A designation under  section 9  has effect, subject to  subsections (2)  to
(5) , during the period—

10.1.a

beginning at the time when it is made, and

10.1.b

ending with a date or at a time specified in the designation.

10.2

The date or time specified under  subsection (1) (b)  must not be later than
the end of the period of 14 days beginning with the day on which the
designation is made.

10.3

A constable may extend from time to time the period during which a designation
has effect.

10.4

An extension under  subsection (3)  must—

10.4.a

be in writing, and

10.4.b

specify the additional period during which the designation is to have effect.

10.5

An extension under  subsection (3)  must not provide for a designation to have
effect after the end of the period of 28 days beginning with the day on which
the designation is made.

##### Powers of police in relation to a cordoned area

11

11.1

A constable may order—

11.1.a

a person not to do any of the following (whether in person or by electronic or
remote means)—

11.1.a.i

enter, inspect, pass over or under, approach or be in the vicinity of a
cordoned area, or

11.1.a.ii

cause an unmanned vehicle or device to enter, inspect, pass over or under,
approach or be in the vicinity of a cordoned area;

11.1.b

a person in a cordoned area (whether in person or by electronic or remote
means) to leave it immediately;

11.1.c

a person in an area adjacent to a cordoned area to leave the area immediately;

11.1.d

the driver or person in charge of a vehicle or device (whether in person or by
electronic or remote means) in a cordoned area to move the vehicle or device
from the area immediately.

11.2

In  subsection (1)  a reference to inspecting a cordoned area includes taking
or procuring the taking of photographs, videos or other recordings.

11.3

A constable may arrange for—

11.3.a

the removal of a vehicle or device from a cordoned area;

11.3.b

the movement of a vehicle or device within a cordoned area.

11.4

A person commits an offence if the person fails to comply with an order
imposed under  subsection (1) .

11.5

It is a defence for a person charged with an offence under  subsection (4)  to
show that the person had a reasonable excuse for that failure.

11.6

A person is taken to have shown a matter mentioned in subsection  (5)  if—

11.6.a

sufficient evidence of the matter is adduced to raise an issue with respect to
it, and

11.6.b

the contrary is not proved beyond reasonable doubt.

11.7

A person who commits an offence under  subsection (4)  is liable on summary
conviction to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 3 months or a fine not
exceeding level 4 on the standard scale (or both).

11.8

In  this section  “ cordoned area ” means an area designated as a cordoned
area under  section 9 .

#### Sabotage

##### Sabotage

12

12.1

A person commits an offence if—

12.1.a

the person engages in conduct that results in damage to any asset,

12.1.b

the person intends their conduct to result in damage to an asset, or is
reckless as to whether their conduct will result in damage to an asset,

12.1.c

the person’s conduct is for a purpose that they know, or having regard to
other matters known to them ought reasonably to know, is prejudicial to the
safety or interests of the United Kingdom, and

12.1.d

the foreign power condition is met in relation to the person’s conduct (see
section  31 ).

12.2

Subsection (1)  applies—

12.2.a

whether the person’s conduct takes place in the United Kingdom or elsewhere;

12.2.b

whether the asset is in the United Kingdom or elsewhere.

12.3

In  this section —

                                    “ asset ” means an asset of any kind
whether tangible or intangible and includes in particular real and personal
property, electronic systems and information;
“ damage ” includes any of the following (whether permanent or temporary)—
destruction;
alteration;
contamination;
interference;
loss of or reduction in access or availability;
loss of or reduction in function, utility or reliability.

12.4

A person who commits an offence under  this section  is liable on conviction
on indictment to imprisonment for life or a fine (or both).

#### Foreign interference

##### Foreign interference: general

13

13.1

A person commits an offence if—

13.1.a

the person engages in prohibited conduct,

13.1.b

the foreign power condition is met in relation to the prohibited conduct, and

13.1.c

the person intends the prohibited conduct, or a course of conduct of which it
forms part, to have an interference effect.

13.2

A person commits an offence if—

13.2.a

the person engages in prohibited conduct,

13.2.b

the foreign power condition is met in relation to the prohibited conduct, and

13.2.c

the person is reckless as to whether the prohibited conduct, or a course of
conduct of which it forms part, will have an interference effect.

13.3

A person (“ P ”) commits an offence if—

13.3.a

P engages in a course of conduct with one or more other persons,

13.3.b

the foreign power condition is met in relation to conduct of P which forms
part of the course of conduct,

13.3.c

P intends the course of conduct to have an interference effect,

13.3.d

as part of the course of conduct, a person other than P engages in prohibited
conduct, and

13.3.e

P intends or believes that, as part of the course of conduct, a person other
than P will engage in prohibited conduct.

13.4

For the purposes of subsections  (1) (c)  and  (2) (c)  a course of conduct
includes a course of conduct engaged in by the person alone, or by the person
and one or more other persons.

13.5

Subsections  (1)  and  (2)  apply whether the person’s conduct takes place in
the United Kingdom or elsewhere.

13.6

Subsection  (3)  applies whether P’s conduct or the prohibited conduct takes
place in the United Kingdom or elsewhere.

13.7

A person who commits an offence under  this section  is liable on conviction
on indictment to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 14 years or a fine (or
both).

13.8

In  this section —

                                    “ interference effect ” has the meaning
given by section  14 ;
“ prohibited conduct ” has the meaning given by section  15 .

##### Foreign interference: meaning of “interference effect”

14

14.1

For the purposes of section  13  an “ interference effect ” means any of the
following effects—

14.1.a

interfering with the exercise by a particular person of a Convention right in
the United Kingdom,

14.1.b

affecting the exercise by any person of their public functions,

14.1.c

interfering with whether, or how, any person makes use of services provided in
the exercise of public functions,

14.1.d

interfering with whether, or how, any person (other than in the exercise of a
public function) participates in relevant political processes or makes
political decisions,

14.1.e

interfering with whether, or how, any person (other than in the exercise of a
public function) participates in legal processes under the law of the United
Kingdom, or

14.1.f

prejudicing the safety or interests of the United Kingdom.

14.2

An effect may be an interference effect whether it relates to a specific
instance of a matter mentioned in subsection  (1) , or to the matter in
general.

14.3

In subsection  (1) (d)  “ relevant political processes ” means—

14.3.a

an election or referendum in the United Kingdom,

14.3.b

the proceedings of a local authority,

14.3.c

the proceedings of a UK registered political party, or

14.3.d

the activities of an informal group consisting of or including members of—

14.3.d.i

one or both of Houses of Parliament,

14.3.d.ii

the Northern Ireland Assembly,

14.3.d.iii

the Scottish Parliament, or

14.3.d.iv

Senedd Cymru,

(acting in that capacity).

14.4

In subsection  (1) (d)  “ political decisions ” means decisions of—

14.4.a

a Minister of the Crown (within the meaning of the Ministers of the Crown Act
1975) or a United Kingdom government department,

14.4.b

a Northern Ireland Minister, the First Minister in Northern Ireland, the
deputy First Minister in Northern Ireland, a person appointed as a junior
Minister under section 19 of the Northern Ireland Act 1998, a Northern Ireland
department or the Executive Committee of the Northern Ireland Assembly,

14.4.c

the Scottish Ministers or the First Minister for Scotland,

14.4.d

the Welsh Ministers, the First Minister for Wales or the Counsel General to
the Welsh Government, or

14.4.e

a local authority.

14.5

In  this section —

                                    “ Convention rights ” has the meaning
given by section 1 of the Human Rights Act 1998;
the “ law of the United Kingdom ” includes the law of any part of the United
Kingdom;
“ local authority ” means—
in England—
a county council;
a district council;
a London borough council;
a combined authority established under section 103 of the Local Democracy,
Economic Development and Construction Act 2009;
a parish council;
the Council of the Isles of Scilly;
the Common Council of the City of London;
the Sub-Treasurer of the Inner Temple;
the Under Treasurer of the Middle Temple;
in Wales, a county council, county borough council or community council;
in Scotland, a council constituted under section 2 of the Local Government
etc. (Scotland) Act 1994;
in Northern Ireland, a district council;
“ public functions ” means functions of a public nature—
exercisable in the United Kingdom, or
exercisable in a country or territory outside the United Kingdom by a person
acting for or on behalf of, or holding office under, the Crown;
“ UK registered political party ” means a political party registered under
Part 2 of the Political Parties, Elections and Referendums Act 2000.

##### Foreign interference: meaning of “prohibited conduct”

15

15.1

Conduct is prohibited conduct for the purposes of section  13  if—

15.1.a

it constitutes an offence, or

15.1.b

if it takes place in a country or territory outside the United Kingdom, it
would constitute an offence if it took place in any part of the United
Kingdom.

15.2

Conduct is prohibited conduct for the purposes of section  13  if it involves
coercion of any kind, including coercion by—

15.2.a

using or threatening to use violence against a person;

15.2.b

damaging or destroying, or threatening to damage or destroy, a person’s
property;

15.2.c

damaging or threatening to damage a person’s reputation;

15.2.d

causing or threatening to cause financial loss to a person;

15.2.e

causing spiritual injury to, or placing undue spiritual pressure on, a person;

(whether or not that person is the person to whom the interference effect
relates).

15.3

Conduct is prohibited conduct for the purposes of section  13  if it involves
making a misrepresentation.

15.4

A “misrepresentation” is a representation—

15.4.a

that a reasonable person would consider to be false or misleading in a way
material to the interference effect, and

15.4.b

that the person making the representation knows or intends to be false or
misleading in a way material to the interference effect.

15.5

A misrepresentation may be made by making a statement or by any other kind of
conduct, and may be express or implied.

15.6

A misrepresentation may in particular include—

15.6.a

a misrepresentation as to a person’s identity or purpose;

15.6.b

presenting information in a way which amounts to a misrepresentation, even if
some or all of the information is true.

15.7

In this section “ interference effect ” has the meaning given by section  14 .

##### Foreign interference in elections

16

16.1

This section  applies where—

16.1.a

a person commits a relevant electoral offence on or after the day on which
this section  comes into force, and

16.1.b

the foreign power condition is met in relation to the conduct of the person
which constitutes the offence (see section  31 ).

16.2

A “relevant electoral offence” is an offence listed in column 1 of the table
in  Part 1  of  Schedule 1  (“the table”).

16.3

The person is liable on conviction on indictment to imprisonment for a term
not exceeding the specified maximum term or a fine (or both).

16.4

The specified maximum term is the term specified in column 2 of the table in
relation to the relevant electoral offence.

16.5

Where an offence is found to have been committed over a period of 2 or more
days, or at some time during a period of 2 or more days, it must be taken for
the purposes of  subsection (1)  to have been committed on the first of those
days.

16.6

Part 2  of  Schedule 1  amends provisions relating to relevant electoral
offences.

#### Obtaining benefits from a foreign intelligence service

##### Obtaining etc material benefits from a foreign intelligence service

17

17.1

A person commits an offence if—

17.1.a

the person—

17.1.a.i

obtains, accepts or retains a material benefit which is not an excluded
benefit, or

17.1.a.ii

obtains or accepts the provision of such a benefit to another person,

17.1.b

the benefit is or was provided by or on behalf of a foreign intelligence
service, and

17.1.c

the person knows, or having regard to other matters known to them ought
reasonably to know, that the benefit is or was provided by or on behalf of a
foreign intelligence service.

17.2

A person commits an offence if—

17.2.a

the person agrees to accept—

17.2.a.i

a material benefit which is not an excluded benefit, or

17.2.a.ii

the provision of such a benefit to another person,

17.2.b

the benefit is to be provided by or on behalf of a foreign intelligence
service, and

17.2.c

the person knows, or having regard to other matters known to them ought
reasonably to know, that the benefit is to be provided by or on behalf of a
foreign intelligence service.

17.3

Material benefits may include financial benefits, anything which has the
potential to result in a financial benefit, and information.

17.4

A material benefit is an excluded benefit if—

17.4.a

it is provided as reasonable consideration for the provision of goods or
services, and

17.4.b

the provision of those goods or services does not constitute an offence.

17.5

A benefit may be provided by or on behalf of a foreign intelligence service
directly or indirectly (for example, it may be provided indirectly through one
or more companies).

17.6

Subsections  (1)  and  (2)  apply to conduct outside the United Kingdom, but
apply to conduct taking place wholly outside the United Kingdom only if—

17.6.a

the material benefit is or was, or is to be, provided in or from the United
Kingdom, or

17.6.b

in any case, the person engaging in the conduct—

17.6.b.i

is a UK person, or

17.6.b.ii

acts for or on behalf of, or holds office under, the Crown, or is in Crown
employment (whether or not they engage in the conduct in that capacity).

17.7

In proceedings for an offence under subsection  (1)  by virtue of retaining a
benefit, it is a defence to show that the person had a reasonable excuse for
retaining the benefit.

17.8

In proceedings for an offence under subsection  (1)  or  (2)  it is a defence
to show that the person engaged in the conduct in question—

17.8.a

in compliance with a legal obligation under the law of the United Kingdom
which is not a legal obligation under private law,

17.8.b

in the case of a person having functions of a public nature under the law of
the United Kingdom, for the purposes of those functions, or

17.8.c

in accordance with an agreement or arrangement to which—

17.8.c.i

the United Kingdom was a party, or

17.8.c.ii

any person acting for or on behalf of, or holding office under, the Crown was
(in that capacity) a party.

17.9

A person is taken to have shown a matter mentioned in subsection  (7)  or  (8)
if—

17.9.a

sufficient evidence of the matter is adduced to raise an issue with respect to
it, and

17.9.b

the contrary is not proved beyond reasonable doubt.

17.10

A person who commits an offence under subsection  (1)  is liable on conviction
on indictment to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 14 years or a fine (or
both).

17.11

A person who commits an offence under subsection  (2)  is liable on conviction
on indictment to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 10 years or a fine (or
both).

17.12

The following terms have the same meaning as in  section 3 —

                                    “ Crown employment ”;
“ financial benefit ”;
“ foreign intelligence service ”;
the “ law of the United Kingdom ”;
“ UK person ”.

#### Preparatory conduct

##### Preparatory conduct

18

18.1

A person commits an offence if, with the intention of—

18.1.a

committing acts to which this section applies, or

18.1.b

acts to which this section applies being committed by another person,

the person engages in any conduct in preparation for the commission of such
acts.

18.2

It is immaterial whether the person’s intention relates to, or the person’s
conduct is in preparation for, specific acts to which this section applies, or
acts to which this section applies in general.

18.3

This section applies to—

18.3.a

acts which constitute an offence under—

18.3.a.i

section  1  (obtaining or disclosing protected information);

18.3.a.ii

section 2  (obtaining or disclosing trade secrets);

18.3.a.iii

section 4  (entering etc. a prohibited place for a purpose prejudicial to the
UK);

18.3.a.iv

section 12  (sabotage);

18.3.b

acts within  subsection (4)  in relation to which the foreign power condition
is met.

18.4

Acts are within  this subsection  if they—

18.4.a

involve serious violence against a person in the United Kingdom,

18.4.b

endanger the life of a person in the United Kingdom, or

18.4.c

create a serious risk to the health or safety of the public, or a section of
the public, in the United Kingdom.

18.5

Subsection (1)  applies whether the person’s conduct takes place in the United
Kingdom or elsewhere.

18.6

A person who commits an offence under  this section  is liable on conviction
on indictment to imprisonment for life or a fine (or both).

#### Acting for foreign power as aggravating factor in sentencing

##### Aggravating factor where foreign power condition met: England and Wales

19

19.1

The Sentencing Code is amended as follows.

19.2

After section 69 insert—

########### Offences where foreign power condition met

19.2.69A

19.2.69A.1

This section applies where a court is considering the seriousness of an
offence that—

19.2.69A.1.a

is committed on or after the day on which section  19  of the National
Security Act 2023 comes into force, and

19.2.69A.1.b

is not an offence listed in subsection  (2) .

19.2.69A.2.a

an offence under the National Security Act 2023 or an inchoate offence (see

Act (foreign interference in elections).

19.2.69A.3

Where the foreign power condition is met in relation to the conduct that
constitutes the offence, the court—

19.2.69A.3.a

must treat that fact as an aggravating factor, and

19.2.69A.3.b

must state in open court that the offence is so aggravated.

Where an offence is found to have been committed over a period of 2 or more

##### Aggravating factor where foreign power condition met: Northern Ireland

20

20.1

This section  applies where a court in Northern Ireland is considering for the
purposes of sentence the seriousness of an offence that—

20.1.a

is committed on or after the day on which  this section  comes into force, and

20.1.b

is not an offence listed in  subsection (2) .

20.2

Those offences are—

20.2.a

an offence under this Act or an ancillary offence in relation to any such
offence;

20.2.b

a relevant electoral offence (within the meaning given by section  16 ).

20.3

An “ ancillary offence ”, in relation to an offence, means any of the
following—

20.3.a

aiding, abetting, counselling or procuring the commission of the offence;

20.3.b

an offence under Part 2 of the Serious Crime Act 2007 (encouraging or
assisting crime) in relation to the offence;

20.3.c

attempting or conspiring to commit the offence.

20.4

For the purposes of  this section , an offence committed by a person under
Part 2 of the Serious Crime Act 2007 is related to another offence if that
other offence is the offence (or one of the offences) which the person
intended or believed would be committed.

20.5

Where the foreign power condition is met in relation to the conduct that
constitutes the offence, the court—

20.5.a

must treat that fact as an aggravating factor, and

20.5.b

must state in open court that the offence is so aggravated.

20.6

Where an offence is found to have been committed over a period of 2 or more
days, or at some time during a period of 2 or more days, it must be taken for
the purposes of  subsection (1)  to have been committed on the first of those
days.

20.7

In  this section  “ sentence ”, in relation to an offence, includes any order
made by a court when dealing with a person in respect of the offence.

##### Aggravating factor where foreign power condition met: Scotland

21

21.1

This section  applies where in Scotland, in relation to a relevant offence, it
is—

21.1.a

libelled in an indictment, and

21.1.b

proved,

that the offence has been aggravated by reason of the foreign power condition
being met in relation to the conduct that constitutes the offence.

21.2

Where  this section  applies, the court must take the aggravation into account
in determining the appropriate sentence.

21.3

Where the sentence imposed by the court in respect of the offence is different
from that which the court would have imposed if the offence had not been
aggravated by reason of being an offence within  subsection (1) , the court
must state the extent of, and the reasons for, the difference.

21.4

Evidence from a single source is sufficient to prove that an offence has been
aggravated by reason of the foreign power condition being met in relation to
conduct which constitutes the offence.

21.5

A “relevant offence” is an offence that—

21.5.a

is committed on or after the day on which  this section  comes into force, and

21.5.b

is not an offence listed in  subsection (6) .

21.6

Those offences are—

21.6.a

an offence under this Act or an ancillary offence in relation to any such
offence;

21.6.b

a relevant electoral offence (within the meaning given by section  16 ).

21.7

An “ ancillary offence ”, in relation to an offence, means any of the
following—

21.7.a

being art and part in the commission of the offence;

21.7.b

inciting a person to commit the offence;

21.7.c

attempting or conspiring to commit the offence.

21.8

Where an offence is found to have been committed over a period of 2 or more
days, or at some time during a period of 2 or more days, it must be taken for
the purposes of  subsection (5) (a)  to have been committed on the first of
those days.

##### Arrest without warrant

27

27.1

A constable may arrest without a warrant anyone who the constable reasonably
suspects is, or has been, involved in foreign power threat activity.

27.2

Schedule 6  makes provision about detention under  this section .

27.3

Subject to  subsections (5)  to  (8) , a person detained under  this section
must be released (unless detained under any other power) not later than the
end of the period of 48 hours beginning with—

27.3.a

the time of the person’s arrest under  this section , or

27.3.b

if the person was being detained under a provision listed in  subsection (4)
when arrested under  this section , with the time when the person was detained
under that provision.

27.4

Those provisions are—

27.4.a

section 24 of the Police and Criminal Evidence Act 1984;

27.4.b

Article 26 of the Police and Criminal Evidence (Northern Ireland) Order 1989 (
S.I. 1989/1341 (N.I. 12) );

27.4.c

section 41 of, and Schedule 7 to, the Terrorism Act 2000;

27.4.d

section 1 of the  Criminal Justice (Scotland) Act 2016 (asp 1) ;

27.4.e

Part 1 of Schedule 3 to the Counter-Terrorism and Border Security Act 2019.

27.5

A person arrested under  this section  must be released if, on a review of the
person’s detention under  Part 5  of  Schedule 6 , the review officer does not
authorise continued detention.

This subsection  does not apply if the person is detained in accordance with
subsection (6)  or  (7)  or under any other power.

27.6

Where a police officer intends to make an application for a warrant under
paragraph 37  of  Schedule 6  (warrant of further detention) to extend the
period of a person’s detention, the person may be detained pending the making
of the application.

27.7

Where an application has been made—

27.7.a

under  paragraph 37  of  Schedule 6  for a warrant to extend the period of a
person’s detention, or

27.7.b

under paragraph  44  of that Schedule to further extend the period of a
person’s detention,

the person may be detained pending the conclusion of proceedings on the
application.

27.8

Where an application under  paragraph 37  or  44  of  Schedule 6  is granted
in respect of a person’s detention, the person may be detained, subject to
paragraph 45  of that Schedule (conditions for detention), during the period
specified in the warrant.

27.9

The refusal of an application in respect of a person’s detention under
paragraph 37  or  44  of  Schedule 6  does not prevent the person’s continued
detention in accordance with  this section .

27.10

Subsection (11)  applies where—

27.10.a

a person is detained under  this section  in hospital, or

27.10.b

a person detained under  this section  is removed to hospital because the
person needs medical treatment.

27.11

Where this subsection applies—

27.11.a

any time during which the person is being questioned in hospital or (where
this subsection applies by virtue of  subsection (10) (b) ) on the way there
or back for the purpose of obtaining relevant evidence is to be included in
calculating any period which falls to be calculated for the purposes of  this
section  or  Part 6  of  Schedule 6 , but

27.11.b

any other time when the person is in hospital or (where this subsection
applies by virtue of  subsection (10) (b) ) on the way there or back is not to
be included.

27.12

In  subsection (11)  “ relevant evidence ” means, in relation to the detained
person, evidence which indicates that the detained person is, or has been,
involved in foreign power threat activity.

27.13

A person who has the powers of a constable in one part of the United Kingdom
may exercise the power under  subsection (1)  in any part of the United
Kingdom.

27.14

In  this section  and  Schedule 6  references to involvement in foreign power
threat activity do not include involvement in such activity occurring before
this section  comes into force.

28.1.b

##### Offences under Part 2 of the Serious Crime Act 2007

30

30.1

Part 2 of the Serious Crime Act 2007 (encouraging or assisting crime) is
amended as follows.

30.2

After section 50 insert—

########### Extra-territorial offences: defence for intelligence services and armed forces

30.2.50A

30.2.50A.1

This section applies where a person is charged with an offence under this Part
by reason of a provision of Schedule 4 (extra-territorial jurisdiction).

30.2.50A.2

It is a defence for the person to show that their act was necessary for—

30.2.50A.2.a

the proper exercise of a function of an intelligence service, or

30.2.50A.2.b

the proper exercise of a function of the armed forces relating to
intelligence.

30.2.50A.3

A person is taken to have shown that their act was so necessary if—

30.2.50A.3.a

sufficient evidence of that fact is adduced to raise an issue with respect to
it, and

30.2.50A.3.b

the contrary is not proved beyond reasonable doubt.

30.2.50A.4

The head of each intelligence service must ensure that the service has in
place arrangements designed to ensure that acts of a member of the service to
which a provision of Schedule 4 applies are necessary for the proper exercise
of a function of the service.

30.2.50A.5

The Defence Council must ensure that the armed forces have in place
arrangements designed to ensure that acts of—

30.2.50A.5.a

a member of the armed forces, or

30.2.50A.5.b

a civilian subject to service discipline when working in support of a member
of the armed forces,

to which a provision of Schedule 4 applies are necessary for the proper
exercise of a function of the armed forces relating to intelligence.

30.2.50A.6

The arrangements which must be in place by virtue of subsection  (4)  or  (5)
must be arrangements which the Secretary of State considers to be
satisfactory.

30.2.50A.7

In this section—

            “ armed forces ” means His Majesty’s forces (within the meaning of
the Armed Forces Act 2006);
“ civilian subject to service discipline ” has the same meaning as in the
Armed Forces Act 2006;
“ GCHQ ” has the meaning given by section 3(3) of the Intelligence Services
Act 1994;
“ head ” means—
in relation to the Security Service, the Director General of the Security
Service,
in relation to the Secret Intelligence Service, the Chief of the Secret
Intelligence Service, and
in relation to GCHQ, the Director of GCHQ;
“ intelligence service ” means the Security Service, the Secret Intelligence
Service or GCHQ.

30.3

For the heading before section 50 substitute  “Defences” .

#### Foreign power condition and foreign power threat activity

##### The foreign power condition

31

31.1

For the purposes of this Part the foreign power condition is met in relation
to a person’s conduct if—

31.1.a

the conduct in question, or a course of conduct of which it forms part, is
carried out for or on behalf of a foreign power, and

31.1.b

the person knows, or having regard to other matters known to them ought
reasonably to know, that to be the case.

31.2

The conduct in question, or a course of conduct of which it forms part, is in
particular to be treated as carried out for or on behalf of a foreign power
if—

31.2.a

it is instigated by a foreign power,

31.2.b

it is under the direction or control of a foreign power,

31.2.c

it is carried out with financial or other assistance provided by a foreign
power for that purpose, or

31.2.d

it is carried out in collaboration with, or with the agreement of, a foreign
power.

31.3

Subsections (1) (a)  and  (2)  may be satisfied by a direct or indirect
relationship between the conduct, or the course of conduct, and the foreign
power (for example, there may be an indirect relationship through one or more
companies).

31.4

A person’s conduct may form part of a course of conduct engaged in by the
person alone, or by the person and one or more other persons.

31.5

The foreign power condition is also met in relation to a person’s conduct if
the person intends the conduct in question to benefit a foreign power.

31.6

For the purposes of  subsection (5)  it is not necessary to identify a
particular foreign power.

31.7

The foreign power condition may be met in relation to the conduct of a person
who holds office in or under, or is an employee or other member of staff of, a
foreign power, as it may be met in relation to the conduct of any other
person.

##### Meaning of “foreign power”

32

32.1

In this Part “ foreign power ” means—

32.1.a

the sovereign or other head of a foreign State in their public capacity,

32.1.b

a foreign government, or part of a foreign government,

32.1.c

an agency or authority of a foreign government, or of part of a foreign
government,

32.1.d

an authority responsible for administering the affairs of an area within a
foreign country or territory, or persons exercising the functions of such an
authority, or

32.1.e

a political party which is a governing political party of a foreign
government.

32.2

A political party is a governing political party of a foreign government if
persons holding political or official posts in the foreign government or part
of the foreign government—

32.2.a

hold those posts as a result of, or in the course of, their membership of the
party, or

32.2.b

in exercising the functions of those posts, are subject to the direction or
control of, or significantly influenced by, the party.

32.3

Subsection (1) (e)  does not include a political party which is—

32.3.a

a governing political party of the government of the Republic of Ireland, and

32.3.b

a party registered under Part 2 of the Political Parties, Elections and
Referendums Act 2000.

32.4

In  this section —

                                    “ foreign country or territory ” means a
country or territory outside the United Kingdom, the Channel Islands, the Isle
of Man or the British Overseas Territories;
“ foreign government ” means the government of a foreign country or territory;
a “ government ” includes persons exercising the functions of a government;
“ territory ” includes the constituent territories of a federal State.

##### Foreign power threat activity and involvement in that activity

33

33.1

In this Part references to foreign power threat activity and to involvement in
foreign power threat activity are to one or more of the following—

33.1.a

the commission, preparation or instigation of acts or threats within
subsection (3) ;

33.1.b

conduct which facilitates (or is intended to facilitate) conduct falling
within  paragraph (a) ;

33.1.c

conduct which gives support or assistance to a person (“ P ”), where the
person who engages in the conduct—

33.1.c.i

knows or believes P to be involved in, and

33.1.c.ii

engages in the conduct for the purpose of giving support or assistance to,

conduct falling within paragraph (a).

33.2

It is immaterial whether the activity within  subsection (1)  relates to
specific acts or threats within  subsection (3) , or to acts or threats within
that subsection in general.

33.3

References to acts or threats within  this subsection  are to—

33.3.a

acts which constitute an offence under—

33.3.a.i

section 1  (obtaining or disclosing protected information);

33.3.a.ii

section 2  (obtaining or disclosing trade secrets);

33.3.a.iii

section 3  (assisting a foreign intelligence service);

33.3.a.iv

section 4  (entering etc. a prohibited place for a purpose prejudicial to the
UK);

33.3.a.v

section 12  (sabotage);

33.3.a.vi

section  13  (foreign interference: general);

33.3.a.vii

section  17 (1)  (obtaining material benefits from a foreign intelligence
service);

33.3.b

acts within  subsection (4)  in relation to which the foreign power condition
is met;

33.3.c

threats to carry out acts within  subsection (4) , where the foreign power
condition is met in relation to the threats.

33.4

Acts are within  this subsection  if they—

33.4.a

involve serious violence against another person,

33.4.b

endanger the life of another person, or

33.4.c

create a serious risk to the health or safety of the public or a section of
the public.

#### Supplementary provision

##### Interpretation

34

34.1

In  this Part —

                                    “ conduct ” includes omissions and
statements;
“ enactment ” includes—
an enactment comprised in subordinate legislation (within the meaning of the
Interpretation Act 1978);
an enactment comprised in, or in an instrument made under, a Measure or Act of
Senedd Cymru;
an enactment comprised in, or in an instrument made under, an Act of the
Scottish Parliament;
an enactment comprised in, or in an instrument made under, Northern Ireland
legislation;
retained direct EU legislation;
“ foreign power ” has the meaning given by section  32 ;
“ the foreign power condition ” has the meaning given by section  31 ;
“ foreign power threat activity ” and “ involvement ”, in relation to such
activity, have the meaning given by section  33 ;
“ information ” includes information about tactics, techniques and procedures;
“ the maximum term for summary offences ” means—
in relation to an offence committed before the time when section 281(5) of the
Criminal Justice Act 2003 comes into force, 6 months;
in relation to an offence committed after that time, 51 weeks.

34.2

In  this Part  references to a part of the United Kingdom are references to—

34.2.a

England and Wales,

34.2.b

Scotland, or

34.2.c

Northern Ireland.

##### Offences by bodies corporate etc

35

35.1

If an offence under this Part is committed by a body—

35.1.a

with the consent or connivance of an officer of the body, or

35.1.b

due to any neglect on the part of such an officer,

the officer, as well as the body, is guilty of the offence and liable to be
proceeded against and punished accordingly.

35.2

In this section—

                                    “ body ” means a body corporate, a
partnership or an unincorporated association other than a partnership;
“ officer of a body ”—
in relation to a body corporate, means a director, member of the committee of
management, chief executive, manager, secretary or other similar officer of
the body, or a person purporting to act in any such capacity;
in relation to a partnership, means a partner or person purporting to act as a
partner;
in relation to an unincorporated association other than a partnership, means a
person who is concerned in the management or control of the body or purports
to act in the capacity of a person so concerned.

35.3

In  subsection (2)  “ director ” includes—

35.3.a

a person occupying in relation to a body corporate the position of a director
(by whatever name called),

35.3.b

a person in accordance with whose directions or instructions (not being advice
given in a professional capacity) the directors of that body are accustomed to
act, and

35.3.c

a person who has an interest or right in, or in relation to, the body
corporate that (whether alone or together with other interests or rights held
by the person) enables the person materially to influence the policy of the
body corporate.

35.4

If the affairs of a body corporate are managed by its members,  subsection (1)
applies in relation to the acts and defaults of a member in connection with
the member's functions of management as if the member were a director of the
body.

35.5

The Secretary of State may by regulations provide for the modification of any
provision of this section in its application to a body corporate or
unincorporated association formed or recognised under the law of a country or
territory outside the United Kingdom.

##### Offences committed outside the United Kingdom

36

36.1

Where an offence under this Part may be committed by conduct taking place
outside the United Kingdom, it may be so committed—

36.1.a

in the case of conduct by an individual, whatever the nationality of the
individual, and

36.1.b

in the case of conduct by a person other than an individual, regardless of
whether the body corporate or unincorporated association is formed or
recognised under the law of a country or territory outside the United Kingdom.

36.2

Subsection (1)  is subject to sections  3 (6)  and  17 (6)  (commission of
offences under sections  3  and  17  by conduct outside the United Kingdom).

36.3

Where an offence under this Part is committed outside the United Kingdom—

36.3.a

proceedings for the offence may be taken at any place in the United Kingdom,
and

36.3.b

the offence may for all incidental purposes be treated as having been
committed at any such place.

36.4

In the application of subsection  (3)  to Scotland, any such proceedings
against a person may be taken—

36.4.a

in any sheriff court district in which the person is apprehended or is in
custody, or

36.4.b

in such sheriff court district as the Lord Advocate may determine.

36.5

“Sheriff court district”  is to be read in accordance with the Criminal
Procedure (Scotland) Act 1995 (see section 307(1) of that Act).

##### Consents to prosecutions

37

37.1

This section applies to offences under this Part, except offences under—

37.1.a

section  5  (unauthorised entry to a prohibited place);

37.1.b

section  6  (prohibited place: failure to comply with order of constable);

37.1.c

section 11  (cordoned area: failure to comply with order of constable);

37.1.d

Schedule 2  (powers of entry, search and seizure);

37.1.e

Schedule  3  (disclosure orders);

37.1.f

Schedule  4  (customer information orders).

37.2

Proceedings for an offence to which this section applies may be instituted—

37.2.a

in England and Wales, only with the consent of the Attorney General;

37.2.b

in Northern Ireland, only with the consent of the Advocate General for
Northern Ireland.

##### Power to exclude the public from proceedings

38

If it is necessary in the interests of national security, a court may exclude
the public from—

38.a

any part of proceedings for an offence under this Part, or

38.b

any part of proceedings relating to section 69A of the Sentencing Act 2020 (as
inserted by section  19 ) or to section  20  or  21 ,

except for the passing of sentence.

### Prevention and investigation measures

#### Imposition of prevention and investigation measures

##### Power to impose prevention and investigation measures

39

39.1

The Secretary of State may by notice (a “ Part 2  notice”) impose specified
prevention and investigation measures on an individual if conditions A to E in
section 40  are met.

39.2

In this Part “ prevention and investigation measures ” means requirements,
restrictions and other provision which may be made in relation to an
individual by virtue of  Schedule 7 .

39.3

In  this section  and  Part 1  of  Schedule 7  “ specified ” means specified
in the  Part 2  notice.

39.4

The Secretary of State must publish factors that the Secretary of State
considers are appropriate to take into account when deciding whether to impose
restrictions on an individual by virtue of  paragraph 2  of  Schedule 7
(travel measure).

##### Conditions A to E

40

40.1

Condition A is that the Secretary of State reasonably believes that the
individual is, or has been, involved in foreign power threat activity.

40.2

Condition B is that some or all of the foreign power threat activity in which
the individual is, or has been, involved is new foreign power threat activity.

40.3

Condition C is that the Secretary of State reasonably considers that it is
necessary, for purposes connected with protecting the United Kingdom from the
risk of acts or threats within section  33 (3) , for prevention and
investigation measures to be imposed on the individual.

40.4

Condition D is that the Secretary of State reasonably considers that it is
necessary, for purposes connected with preventing or restricting the
individual's involvement in foreign power threat activity, for the prevention
and investigation measures specified in the notice to be imposed on the
individual.

40.5

Condition E is that—

40.5.a

the court gives the Secretary of State permission under  section 42 , or

40.5.b

the Secretary of State reasonably considers that the urgency of the case
requires prevention and investigation measures to be imposed without obtaining
such permission.

40.6

In relation to prevention and investigation measures under  paragraph 1  of
Schedule 7  (residence measure), conditions A, B and D (and  subsection (7) )
apply as if the references to foreign power threat activity were to foreign
power threat activity which relates to acts or threats within section  33 (3)
(b)  or  (c) .

40.7

In  this section  “ new foreign power threat activity ” means—

40.7.a

if no  Part 2  notice relating to the individual has ever been in force,
foreign power threat activity occurring at any time;

40.7.b

if only one  Part 2  notice relating to the individual has ever been in force,
foreign power threat activity occurring after that notice came into force;

40.7.c

if two or more  Part 2  notices relating to the individual have been in force,
foreign power threat activity occurring after such a notice came into force
most recently.

40.8

In this section references to foreign power threat activity, and to an
individual’s involvement in such activity, include foreign power threat
activity, and an individual’s involvement in such activity, occurring before
section  39  comes into force.

#### Five year limit on imposition of measures

##### Five year limit for 

41

41.1

A  Part 2  notice—

41.1.a

comes into force when the notice is served on the individual or, if later, at
the time specified for this purpose in the notice, and

41.1.b

is in force for the period of one year.

41.2

The Secretary of State may by notice extend a  Part 2  notice for a period of
one year beginning when the  Part 2  notice would otherwise expire.

41.3

A  Part 2  notice—

41.3.a

may be extended under  subsection (2)  only if conditions A, C and D are met,
and

41.3.b

may be so extended on up to four occasions.

41.4

This section  is subject, in particular, to sections  49  (revocation and
revival of  Part 2  notices) and  50  (replacement of  Part 2  notice that is
quashed etc).

#### Court scrutiny of imposition of measures

##### Prior permission of the court

42

42.1

This section  applies if the Secretary of State—

42.1.a

makes the relevant decisions in relation to an individual, and

42.1.b

makes an application to the court for permission to impose measures on the
individual.

42.2

The application must set out a draft of the proposed  Part 2  notice.

42.3

The function of the court on the application is—

42.3.a

to determine whether the relevant decisions of the Secretary of State are
obviously flawed, and

42.3.b

to determine whether to give permission to impose measures on the individual
and (where applicable) whether to exercise the power of direction under
subsection (9) .

42.4

The court may consider the application—

42.4.a

in the absence of the individual,

42.4.b

without the individual having been notified of the application, and

42.4.c

without the individual having been given an opportunity (if the individual was
aware of the application) of making any representations to the court.

42.5

But that does not limit the matters about which rules of court may be made.

42.6

In determining the application, the court must apply the principles applicable
on an application for judicial review.

42.7

In a case where the court determines that a decision of the Secretary of State
that condition A, condition B or condition C is met is obviously flawed, the
court may not give permission under  this section .

42.8

In any other case, the court may give permission under  this section .

42.9

If the court determines that the Secretary of State's decision that condition
D is met is obviously flawed, the court may (in addition to giving permission
under  subsection (8) ) give directions to the Secretary of State in relation
to the measures to be imposed on the individual.

42.10

In  this section  “ relevant decisions ” means the decisions that the
following conditions are met—

42.10.a

condition A,

42.10.b

condition B,

42.10.c

condition C, and

42.10.d

condition D.

##### Urgent cases: reference to the court etc

43

Schedule 8  makes provision about references to the court in urgent cases.

##### Directions hearing

44

44.1

This section  applies if the court—

44.1.a

gives permission under  section 42  for measures to be imposed on an
individual, or

44.1.b

confirms under  paragraph 4 (3)  of  Schedule 8  (whether or not subject to
paragraph 4(2) of that Schedule) a  Part 2  notice which imposes measures on
an individual.

44.2

The court must, at the hearing where it gives the permission or confirms the
notice, give directions for a further hearing (a “directions hearing”)—

44.2.a

which, unless the court otherwise directs (whether in those directions or
subsequently), is to be held within the period of 7 days beginning with the
relevant day, and

44.2.b

which the individual is to have the opportunity to attend.

44.3

In a case where  this section  applies because the court gives permission
under  section 42 , directions given under  subsection (2)  may not be served
on the individual unless the  Part 2  notice has been served on that
individual.

44.4

At the directions hearing, the court must give directions for a further
hearing (a “review hearing”) in relation to the imposition of measures on the
individual.

44.5

Directions under  subsection (4)  must provide for the review hearing to be
held as soon as reasonably practicable.

44.6

In  this section  “ relevant day ” means—

44.6.a

in a case falling within  subsection (1) (a) , the day on which the  Part 2
notice imposing the measures is served on the individual;

44.6.b

in a case falling within  subsection (1) (b) , the day on which the court
confirms the  Part 2  notice.

##### Review hearing

45

45.1

On a review hearing held in compliance with directions under  section 44 (4) ,
the function of the court is to review the decisions of the Secretary of State
that the relevant conditions were met and continue to be met.

45.2

In doing so, the court must apply the principles applicable on an application
for judicial review.

45.3

The court—

45.3.a

must discontinue the review hearing if the individual requests the court to do
so, and

45.3.b

may discontinue the review hearing in any other circumstances.

45.4

The court may not discontinue the review hearing in accordance with
subsection (3) (b)  without giving the Secretary of State and the individual
the opportunity to make representations.

45.5

The court has the following powers (and only those powers) on a review
hearing—

45.5.a

power to quash the  Part 2  notice;

45.5.b

power to quash measures specified in the  Part 2  notice;

45.5.c

power to give directions to the Secretary of State for, or in relation to—

45.5.c.i

the revocation of the  Part 2  notice, or

45.5.c.ii

the variation of measures specified in the  Part 2  notice.

45.6

If the court does not exercise any of its powers under  subsection (5) , the
court must decide that the  Part 2  notice is to continue in force.

45.7

If the court exercises a power under  subsection (5) (b)  or  (c) (ii) , the
court must decide that the  Part 2  notice is to continue in force subject to
that exercise of that power.

45.8

In  this section  “ relevant conditions ” means—

45.8.a

condition A,

45.8.b

condition B,

45.8.c

condition C, and

45.8.d

condition D.

#### Consultation requirements

##### Criminal investigations into foreign power threat activity

46

46.1

The Secretary of State must consult the chief officer of the appropriate
police force about the matter mentioned in  subsection (2)  before—

46.1.a

making an application under  section 42  for permission to impose measures on
an individual, or

46.1.b

imposing measures on an individual in a case to which  section 40 (5) (b)
applies (urgency of the case requires measures to be imposed without obtaining
the permission of the court).

46.2

The matter is whether there is evidence available that could realistically be
used for the purposes of prosecuting the individual for an offence—

46.2.a

within  section 33 (3) (a) , or

46.2.b

relating to acts or threats within  section 33 (3) (b)  or  (c) .

46.3

The “ appropriate police force ” means the police force—

46.3.a

that is investigating the commission of any such offence by the individual, or

46.3.b

by which it appears to the Secretary of State that the commission of any such
offence by the individual would fall to be investigated.

46.4

If the Secretary of State serves a  Part 2  notice on an individual, the
Secretary of State must inform the chief officer of the appropriate police
force—

46.4.a

that the  Part 2  notice has been served, and

46.4.b

that the chief officer must act in accordance with the duty under  subsection
(5) .

46.5

After being informed of the matters mentioned in  subsection (4) , the chief
officer must—

46.5.a

secure that the investigation of the individual's conduct, with a view to a
prosecution of the individual for an offence—

46.5.a.i

within  section 33 (3) (a) , or

46.5.a.ii

relating to acts or threats within  section 33 (3) (b)  or  (c) ,

is kept under review throughout the period the  Part 2  notice is in force,
and

46.5.b

report to the Secretary of State on the review carried out under  paragraph
(a) .

46.6

The chief officer must consult the relevant prosecuting authority before
responding to consultation under  subsection (1) .

46.7

The chief officer must also, to the extent that the chief officer considers it
appropriate to do so, consult the relevant prosecuting authority in carrying
out the duty under  subsection (5) (a) .

46.8

The “relevant prosecuting authority” is—

46.8.a

in the case of offences that would be likely to be prosecuted in England and
Wales, the Director of Public Prosecutions;

46.8.b

in the case of offences that would be likely to be prosecuted in Scotland, the
Lord Advocate;

46.8.c

in the case of offences that would be likely to be prosecuted in Northern
Ireland, the Director of Public Prosecutions for Northern Ireland.

46.9

The duty to consult under  subsection (1)  or  (6)  may be satisfied by
consultation that took place wholly or partly before the passing of this Act.

46.10

In  this section —

                                    “ chief officer ”—
in relation to a police force maintained for a police area in England and
Wales, means the chief officer of police of that force;
in relation to the Police Service of Scotland, means the chief constable of
that Service;
in relation to the Police Service of Northern Ireland, means the Chief
Constable of that Service;
in relation to the National Crime Agency, means the Director General of the
National Crime Agency;
“ police force ” means—
a police force maintained for a police area in England and Wales;
the Police Service of Scotland;
the Police Service of Northern Ireland;
the National Crime Agency.

#### Review of ongoing necessity

##### Review of ongoing necessity

47

During the period that a  Part 2  notice is in force, the Secretary of State
must keep under review whether conditions C and D are met.

#### Changes concerning 

##### Variation of measures

48

48.1

The Secretary of State may by notice (a “ variation notice ”) vary measures
specified in a  Part 2  notice if—

48.1.a

the variation consists of the relaxation or removal of measures,

48.1.b

the variation is made with the consent of the individual, or

48.1.c

the Secretary of State reasonably considers that the variation is necessary
for purposes connected with preventing or restricting the individual's
involvement in foreign power threat activity.

48.2

The Secretary of State may by variation notice vary a relocation measure so as
to substitute a different specified residence if the Secretary of State
reasonably considers that—

48.2.a

the variation is necessary for reasons connected with the efficient and
effective use of resources in relation to the individual, and

48.2.b

the relocation measure (as varied) remains necessary for purposes connected
with preventing or restricting the individual’s involvement in foreign power
threat activity which relates to acts or threats within  section 33 (3) (b)
or  (c) .

48.3

A “relocation measure” is a measure under  paragraph 1 (2)  of  Schedule 7
which requires the individual to reside at a specified residence within
paragraph  1 (3) (b)  of that Schedule (requirement to reside at premises
specified by Secretary of State other than individual's own residence).

48.4

The individual to whom a  Part 2  notice relates may make an application to
the Secretary of State for the variation of measures specified in the notice.

48.5

The Secretary of State must consider an application made under  subsection (4)
.

48.6

An application under  subsection (4)  must be made in writing.

48.7

The Secretary of State may by notice request the provision, within such period
of time as the notice may specify, of further information from the individual
in connection with an application under  subsection (4) .

48.8

The Secretary of State is not required to consider an application further
unless any information requested under  subsection (7)  is provided in
accordance with the notice mentioned in that subsection.

48.9

A variation under  subsection (1)  or  (2)  takes effect when the variation
notice is served or, if later, at the time specified for this purpose in the
variation notice.

48.10

The power under  subsection (1)  or  (2)  is exercisable whether or not an
application has been made under  subsection (4) .

48.11

In a case where a  Part 2  notice—

48.11.a

has expired as mentioned in  section 49 (6) (a) , or

48.11.b

has been revoked,

the power under  subsection (1)  or  (2)  may (in particular) be exercised in
relation to the  Part 2  notice before any revival of the  Part 2  notice
under  section 49 (6)  so as to take effect at the time that the  Part 2
notice comes back into force on its revival.

48.12

In such a case, the question of whether condition D is met is to be determined
for the purposes of  section 49 (6)  by reference to the measures specified in
the  Part 2  notice as they would be after the exercise of the power under
subsection (1)  or  (2) .

48.13

Subsection (2)  does not limit the power under  subsection (1) .

##### Revocation and revival of 

49

49.1

The Secretary of State may by notice (a “revocation notice”) revoke a  Part 2
notice at any time.

49.2

The revocation of a  Part 2  notice takes effect when the revocation notice is
served or, if different, at the time specified for this purpose in the
revocation notice.

49.3

The individual to whom a  Part 2  notice relates may make an application to
the Secretary of State for the revocation of the  Part 2  notice.

49.4

The Secretary of State must consider an application made under  subsection (3)
.

49.5

The power under  subsection (1)  is exercisable whether or not an application
has been made under  subsection (3) .

49.6

The Secretary of State may by notice (a “revival notice”) at any time revive a
Part 2  notice which—

49.6.a

has expired—

49.6.a.i

without being extended under  section 41 (2) , or

49.6.a.ii

having been extended under  section 41 (2)  on fewer than four occasions, or

49.6.b

has been revoked,

if conditions A, C and D are met.

49.7

The power of revival may be exercised—

49.7.a

under  subsection (6) (a)  or  (b)  whether or not the  Part 2  notice has
previously been revoked and revived, and

49.7.b

under  subsection (6) (b)  whether or not the  Part 2  notice has been
extended under  section 41 (2)  (and regardless of how many times it has been
so extended).

49.8

But the power of revival under  subsection (6) (b)  may not be exercised to
revive a  Part 2  notice which the Secretary of State was required to revoke
by directions given by the court in relevant proceedings.

49.9

A  Part 2  notice which is revived—

49.9.a

comes back into force when the revival notice is served or, if later, at the
time specified for this purpose in the revival notice,

49.9.b

is in force—

49.9.b.i

for the period of one year (in a case where the revived notice had expired),
or

49.9.b.ii

for the period of time for which the  Part 2  notice would have continued in
force if it had not been revoked (in a case where the revived notice had been
revoked), and

49.9.c

is treated as having been extended under  section 41 (2)  on the same number
of occasions (if any) as on which the revived notice had been so extended.

##### Replacement of a 

50

50.1

This section  applies if—

50.1.a

a  Part 2  notice, the extension of a  Part 2  notice, or the revival of a
Part 2  notice, is quashed in relevant proceedings, or

50.1.b

a  Part 2  notice is revoked by the Secretary of State in compliance with
directions given by the court in relevant proceedings.

50.2

The replacement  Part 2  notice is to be in force for the period of time for
which the overturned notice would have continued in force but for the quashing
or revocation.

50.3

The replacement  Part 2  notice is to be treated as having been extended under
section 41 (2)  on the same number of occasions (if any) as on which the
overturned notice had been so extended (including any extension that was
quashed).

50.4

Foreign power threat activity is to be treated as new foreign power threat
activity in relation to the imposition of measures by the replacement  Part 2
notice if it was new foreign power threat activity in relation to the
imposition of measures by the overturned notice.

50.5

Foreign power threat activity that occurs after the coming into force of the
overturned notice does not cease to be new foreign power threat activity by
virtue of the coming into force of the replacement  Part 2  notice.

50.6

Subsections (2)  to  (5)  do not apply to the replacement notice if—

50.6.a

some or all of the foreign power threat activity occurred after the overturned
notice came into force, and

50.6.b

the Secretary of State determines that those subsections should not apply to
that notice.

50.7

In  this section —

                                    “ new foreign power threat activity ” has
the same meaning as in  section 40 ;
“ overturned notice ” means the  Part 2  notice to which the quashing or
revocation referred to in  subsection (1)  relates;
