“ replacement Part 2 notice ” means the first  Part 2  notice to impose
measures on the individual to whom the overturned notice relates after the
quashing or revocation referred to in  subsection (1) .

##### Other provision relating to the quashing of 

51

51.1

A power in relevant proceedings to quash a  Part 2  notice, the extension of a
Part 2  notice, the revival of a  Part 2  notice, or measures specified in a
Part 2  notice, includes—

51.1.a

in England and Wales or Northern Ireland, power to stay the quashing for a
specified time, or pending an appeal or further appeal against the decision to
quash; or

51.1.b

in Scotland, power to determine that the quashing is of no effect for a
specified time or pending such an appeal or further appeal.

51.2

A decision in relevant proceedings to quash measures specified in a  Part 2
notice, or (except as provided in  section 50 ) a decision in relevant
proceedings to quash, or to give directions to the Secretary of State in
relation to, a  Part 2  notice, the extension of a  Part 2  notice, or the
revival of a  Part 2  notice, does not prevent the Secretary of State—

51.2.a

from exercising any power under this Act to impose measures (whether or not to
the same or similar effect as measures to which the decision relates), or

51.2.b

from relying, in whole or in part, on any matters for the purpose of so
exercising such a power (whether or not the matters were relied on in
exercising powers under this Act in relation to measures or the  Part 2
notice to which the decision relates).

51.3

Schedule 9  makes provision about appeals against convictions.

#### Appeals and court proceedings

##### Appeals

52

52.1

If the Secretary of State extends or revives a  Part 2  notice (see  section
41 (2)  or  49 (6) )—

52.1.a

the individual to whom the  Part 2  notice relates may appeal to the court
against the extension or revival, and

52.1.b

the function of the court on such an appeal is to review the Secretary of
State's decisions that conditions A, C and D were met and continue to be met.

52.2

If the Secretary of State varies measures specified in a  Part 2  notice (and
the variation does not consist of the relaxation or removal of measures)
without the consent of the individual to whom the  Part 2  notice relates—

52.2.a

the individual may appeal to the court against the variation, and

52.2.b

the function of the court on such an appeal is to review the Secretary of
State’s decisions that the variation was necessary, and continues to be
necessary, for purposes connected with preventing or restricting involvement
by the individual in foreign power threat activity.

52.3

If the individual to whom a  Part 2  notice relates makes an application to
the Secretary of State for the variation of measures specified in the  Part 2
notice (see  section 48 (4) )—

52.3.a

the individual may appeal to the court against any decision by the Secretary
of State on the application, and

52.3.b

the function of the court on such an appeal is to review the Secretary of
State’s decisions that the measures to which the application relates were
necessary, and continue to be necessary, for purposes connected with
preventing or restricting involvement by the individual in foreign power
threat activity.

52.4

If the individual to whom a  Part 2  notice relates makes an application to
the Secretary of State for the revocation of the notice (see  section 49 (3)
)—

52.4.a

the individual may appeal to the court against any decision by the Secretary
of State on the application, and

52.4.b

the function of the court on such an appeal is to review the Secretary of
State’s decisions that conditions A, C and D were met and continue to be met.

52.5

If the individual to whom a  Part 2  notice relates makes an application to
the Secretary of State for permission—

52.5.a

the individual may appeal to the court against any decision by the Secretary
of State on the application (including any decision about conditions to which
permission is subject), and

52.5.b

the function of the court on such an appeal is to review the decision.

52.6

In determining the matters mentioned in  subsections (1)  to  (5)  the court
must apply the principles applicable on an application for judicial review.

52.7

The only powers of the court on an appeal under  this section  are—

52.7.a

power to quash the extension or revival of the  Part 2  notice;

52.7.b

power to quash measures specified in the  Part 2  notice;

52.7.c

power to give directions to the Secretary of State for, or in relation to—

52.7.c.i

the revocation of the  Part 2  notice, or

52.7.c.ii

the variation of measures specified in the  Part 2  notice;

52.7.d

power to give directions to the Secretary of State in relation to permission
or conditions to which permission is subject.

52.8

If the court does not exercise any of its powers under  subsection (7) , it
must dismiss the appeal.

52.9

In  this section  “ permission ” means permission for the purposes of measures
specified in a  Part 2  notice (see, in particular,  paragraph 17  of
Schedule 7 ).

##### Jurisdiction in relation to decisions under this Part

53

53.1

Decisions relating to  Part 2  notices are not to be questioned in any legal
proceedings other than—

53.1.a

proceedings in the court, or

53.1.b

proceedings on appeal from such proceedings.

53.2

The court is the appropriate tribunal for the purposes of section 7 of the
Human Rights Act 1998 in relation to proceedings all or any part of which call
a decision relating to a  Part 2  notice into question.

53.3

In this Part “decision relating to a  Part 2  notice” means—

53.3.a

a decision made by the Secretary of State in exercise or performance of any
power or duty under any of  sections 39  to  51  or under  Schedule 7  or
Schedule 8 ;

53.3.b

a decision made by the Secretary of State for the purposes of, or in
connection with, the exercise or performance of any such power or duty;

53.3.c

a decision by a constable to give a direction by virtue of paragraph  4  of
Schedule 7  (movement directions measure) or paragraph  11 (1) (b)  of that
Schedule (reporting measure);

53.3.d

a decision by a polygraph operator to give a direction by virtue of paragraph
12 (1) (c)  of  Schedule 7 ;

53.3.e

a decision by a person to give a direction by virtue of  paragraph 15 (2) (d)
of  Schedule 7  (monitoring measure).

##### Proceedings relating to measures

54

54.1

No appeal lies from any determination of the court in relevant proceedings,
except on a question of law.

54.2

No appeal by any person other than the Secretary of State lies from any
determination—

54.2.a

on an application for permission under  section 42 , or

54.2.b

on a reference under  Schedule 8 .

54.3

Schedule 10  makes provision about proceedings relating to measures.

#### Other safeguards

##### Reports on exercise of powers under this Part

55

55.1

The Secretary of State must—

55.1.a

prepare a report about the exercise of the powers mentioned in  subsection (2)
during each period of 3 months beginning with the month in which section  39
comes into force, and

55.1.b

lay a copy of each such report before Parliament.

55.2

The powers referred to in  subsection (1)  are the powers of the Secretary of
State under this Part—

55.2.a

to impose measures on an individual by a  Part 2  notice;

55.2.b

to extend a  Part 2  notice under  section 41 (2) ;

55.2.c

to vary a  Part 2  notice under  section 48 ;

55.2.d

to revoke a  Part 2  notice under  section 49 (1) ;

55.2.e

to revive a  Part 2  notice under  section 49 (6) .

55.3

The duty under  subsection (1)  in relation to the preparation and laying of a
report must be carried out as soon as reasonably practicable after the end of
the 3 month period to which the report relates.

#### Enforcement

##### Offence

56

56.1

An individual commits an offence if—

56.1.a

a  Part 2  notice is in force in relation to the individual, and

56.1.b

the individual contravenes without reasonable excuse any measure specified in
the notice.

56.2

Where an individual—

56.2.a

is subject to a measure specified under  paragraph 2  of  Schedule 7  (a
“travel measure”), and

56.2.b

leaves the United Kingdom or travels outside the United Kingdom,

subsection (1) (b)  has effect, in relation to that act, with the omission of
the words “without reasonable excuse”.

56.3

If the individual has the permission of the Secretary of State by virtue of
Schedule 7  for an act which would, without that permission, contravene a
measure specified in the  Part 2  notice, the individual contravenes that
measure by virtue of that act if the act is not in accordance with the terms
of the permission.

56.4

An individual who commits an offence under  subsection (1)  is liable—

56.4.a

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 5 years
or to a fine (or both);

56.4.b

on summary conviction in England and Wales, to imprisonment for a term not
exceeding the general limit in a magistrates’ court or to a fine (or both);

56.4.c

on summary conviction in Northern Ireland, to imprisonment for a term not
exceeding 6 months or to a fine not exceeding the statutory maximum (or both);

56.4.d

on summary conviction in Scotland, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 12
months or to a fine not exceeding the statutory maximum (or both).

56.5

Where an individual commits an offence under  subsection (1)  by contravening
a travel measure,  subsection (4) (a)  has effect as if “10 years” were
substituted for “5 years”.

56.6

Where an individual is convicted by or before a court of an offence under
subsection (1) , it is not open to that court to make in respect of the
offence—

56.6.a

an order under section 80 of the Sentencing Code (conditional discharge),

56.6.b

an order under section 227A of the Criminal Procedure (Scotland) Act 1995
(community payback orders), or

56.6.c

an order under Article 4(1)(b) of the Criminal Justice (Northern Ireland)
Order 1996 ( S.I. 1996/3160 (N.I. 24) ) (conditional discharge).

##### Powers of entry etc

57

Schedule 11  makes provision about powers of entry, search, seizure and
retention.

##### Fingerprints and samples

58

Schedule 12  makes provision about fingerprints and samples.

#### Supplementary provisions

##### Notices

59

59.1

In a case where the Secretary of State serves a  Part 2  notice, a revival
notice or an extension notice on an individual, the Secretary of State must,
by a further notice, give the following information to the individual—

59.1.a

the period for which the  Part 2  notice will be in force,

59.1.b

the day on which the  Part 2  notice comes, or came, into force, and

59.1.c

the day on which the  Part 2  notice will expire,

and, in the case of a revival or extension notice, “ Part 2  notice” means the
Part 2  notice which is revived or extended by that notice.

59.2

An individual is not bound by—

59.2.a

a  Part 2  notice,

59.2.b

a revival notice, or

59.2.c

a variation notice insofar as it gives notice of a variation that is neither a
relaxation or removal of measures, nor a variation with the individual's
consent,

unless the notice is served personally on the individual.

59.3

An individual is not bound by an extension notice unless the notice is—

59.3.a

served personally on the individual, and

59.3.b

so served before the  Part 2  notice to which it relates would otherwise
expire.

59.4

Any of the following notices must be served on the individual to whom the
notice relates—

59.4.a

a revocation notice;

59.4.b

a variation notice insofar as  subsection (2) (c)  does not apply to it;

59.4.c

a confirmation notice.

59.5

Any of the following notices may be proved by the production of a document
purporting to be certified by the Secretary of State as a true copy of the
notice—

59.5.a

a  Part 2  notice;

59.5.b

an extension notice;

59.5.c

a revocation notice;

59.5.d

a revival notice;

59.5.e

a variation notice;

59.5.f

a confirmation notice.

59.6

But that does not prevent the proof of such a notice in other ways.

59.7

In  this section —

                                    “ confirmation notice ” means a notice
given under  subsection (1) ;
“ extension notice ” means a notice under  section 41 (2) ;
“ revival notice ” has the same meaning as in  section 49 (6) ;
“ revocation notice ” has the same meaning as in  section 49 (1) ;
“ variation notice ” has the same meaning as in  section 48 (1) .

##### Contracts

60

The Secretary of State may enter into such contracts and other arrangements
with other persons as the Secretary of State considers appropriate for
securing their assistance in connection with any monitoring, by electronic or
other means, that the Secretary of State considers needs to be carried out in
connection with measures specified in  Part 2  notices.

##### Legal aid in relation to Part 2 notices

61

In Schedule 1 to the Legal Aid, Sentencing and Punishment of Offenders Act
2012 (civil legal services), in Part 1 (services), after paragraph 45A insert—

######### Foreign power threat activity prevention and investigation measures

61.45B

61.45B.1

Civil legal services provided to an individual in relation to a notice under
section 39 (1) of the National Security Act 2023 relating to the individual.

61.45B.2

Sub-paragraph (1) is subject to—

61.45B.2.a

the exclusions in Part 2 of this Schedule, with the exception of paragraph 18
of that Part, and

61.45B.2.b

the exclusion in Part 3 of this Schedule.

##### Interpretation etc

62

62.1

In  this Part —

                                    “ act ” and “conduct” include omissions
and statements;
“ condition A ”, “condition B”, “condition C”, “condition D” or “ condition E
” means that condition as set out in  section 40 ;
“ court ” means—
in the case of proceedings relating to an individual whose principal place of
residence is in Scotland, the Outer House of the Court of Session;
in the case of proceedings relating to an individual whose principal place of
residence is in Northern Ireland, the High Court in Northern Ireland;
in any other case, the High Court in England and Wales;
“ decision relating to a Part 2 notice ” has the meaning given in  section 53
;
“ enactment ” includes—
an enactment comprised in subordinate legislation (within the meaning of the
Interpretation Act 1978);
an enactment comprised in, or in an instrument made under, a Measure or Act of
Senedd Cymru;
an enactment comprised in, or in an instrument made under, an Act of the
Scottish Parliament;
an enactment comprised in, or in an instrument made under, Northern Ireland
legislation;
retained direct EU legislation;
“ foreign power threat activity ” and “ involvement ” (in relation to such
activity) have the same meaning as in  Part 1  (see section  33 );
“ measures ” means prevention and investigation measures (which has the
meaning given in  section 39 );
“ notice ” means a notice in writing;
“ Part 2 notice ” has the meaning given in section  39 (1) ;
“ relevant proceedings ” means—
proceedings on an application for permission under  section 42 ;
proceedings on a reference under  Schedule 8 ;
proceedings on a directions hearing held in accordance with directions under
section 44 (2) ;
proceedings on a review hearing held in accordance with directions under
section 44 (4) ;
proceedings on an appeal under  section 52 ;
proceedings by virtue of  section 53 (2) ;
proceedings on an application made by virtue of rules of court made under
paragraph 6  of  Schedule 10  (application for order requiring anonymity);
any other proceedings for questioning a decision relating to a  Part 2  notice
(including any claim for damages or other relief arising out of such a
decision).

62.2

In a case where—

62.2.a

a  Part 2  notice has come into force in relation to an individual, and

62.2.b

by virtue of the coming into force of that  Part 2  notice, foreign power
threat activity which occurred before the coming into force of that notice has
ceased to be new foreign power threat activity (within the meaning of  section
40 (7) ) in relation to that individual for the purposes of that section,

the Secretary of State is not prevented from taking account of that activity
for the purposes of the continued imposition, or subsequent imposition, of
measures on that individual.

62.3

For the purposes of the definition of “new foreign power threat activity” in
section 40 (7) , if a  Part 2  notice is revived under section  49 (6) , a
reference to the notice coming into force is a reference to it coming into
force by virtue of section  41 (1)  (and not to it coming back into force by
virtue of  section 49 (9) ).

62.4

For the purpose of determining what measures may be imposed on an individual,
it is immaterial whether the involvement in foreign power threat activity to
be prevented or restricted by the measures is connected with matters to which
the Secretary of State’s belief for the purpose of condition A relates.

This is subject to  section 40 (6) .

62.5

A failure by the Secretary of State to consider an application by an
individual for—

62.5.a

the revocation of a  Part 2  notice, or

62.5.b

the variation of measures specified in a  Part 2  notice,

is to be treated as a decision by the Secretary of State not to revoke, or not
to vary, the  Part 2  notice.

62.6

Subsections (2)  to  (5)  apply for the purposes of  this Part .

### Review of the operation of Parts 1 and 2 etc

#### Reviews: general

63

63.1

The Secretary of State must appoint a person (the “independent reviewer”) to
review the operation of—

63.1.a

Part 1, except  section 30 ;

63.1.b

Part 2;

63.1.c

Schedule 3 to the Counter-Terrorism and Border Security Act 2019, except the
functions of the Investigatory Powers Commissioner under Part 1 of that
Schedule.

63.2

The independent reviewer—

63.2.a

must carry out a review of the operation of those provisions for each calendar
year (an “annual review”), and

63.2.b

may carry out such other reviews of the operation of any of those provisions
as they consider appropriate.

63.3

An annual review must be completed as soon as reasonably practicable after the
calendar year to which it relates.

63.4

The independent reviewer must, by 31 January in each calendar year, inform the
Secretary of State what (if any) reviews under subsection  (2) (b)  they
intend to carry out in that year.

63.5

The independent reviewer must send to the Secretary of State a report on the
outcome of each review carried out under this section as soon as reasonably
practicable after completion of the review.

63.6

On receiving a report under this section, the Secretary of State must lay
before Parliament—

63.6.a

the report (but not any material removed under subsection  (7) ), and

63.6.b

a statement as to whether any material has been removed under that subsection.

63.7

The Secretary of State may, after consulting the independent reviewer, remove
from the report any material whose publication the Secretary of State thinks
would be contrary to the public interest, or prejudicial to—

63.7.a

national security,

63.7.b

the prevention or detection of crime,

63.7.c

the economic well-being of the United Kingdom, or

63.7.d

the continued discharge of the functions of any public authority whose
activities include activities that are subject to review by the independent
reviewer.

63.8

“ Public authority ” means a public authority within the meaning of section 6
of the Human Rights Act 1998, other than a court or tribunal.

63.9

The Secretary of State may pay to the independent reviewer—

63.9.a

expenses incurred in carrying out the functions of the reviewer under this
section, and

63.9.b

such allowances as the Secretary of State determines.

#### Reviews of detention under 

64

64.1

An annual review under  section 63 (2) (a)  must in particular consider
compliance with the relevant requirements in relation to persons detained
under section  27  by virtue of a warrant of further detention under  Part 6
of  Schedule 6 .

64.2

The relevant requirements are requirements imposed—

64.2.a

by or under Parts  1  to  5 , and  paragraph 45 , of  Schedule 6 ;

64.2.b

by any relevant code of practice under section 66 of the Police and Criminal
Evidence Act 1984 or Article 65 of the Police and Criminal Evidence (Northern
Ireland) Order 1989 ( S.I. 1989/1341 (N.I. 12) ).

64.3

The independent reviewer must ensure that a review is carried out into any
case where—

64.3.a

a person is detained under section  27  by virtue of a warrant of further
detention under  Part 6  of  Schedule 6 , and

64.3.b

the period specified in that warrant is further extended under  paragraph 44
of that Schedule to a time that is more than 14 days after the person’s arrest
under section  27 .

64.4

A review under subsection  (3)  may be carried out by the independent reviewer
or by another person.

64.5

The independent reviewer must ensure that a report on the outcome of a review
under subsection  (3)  is sent to the Secretary of State as soon as reasonably
practicable after completion of the review.

64.6

Section  63 (6)  to  (8)  applies to a report of a review under subsection
(3) .

64.7

The expenses mentioned in section  63 (9)  include any expenses incurred by
the independent reviewer in ensuring that another person carries out, and
reports on, a review under subsection  (3) .

64.8

“ Independent reviewer ” has the same meaning as in section  63 .

### Foreign activities and foreign influence registration scheme

#### Activities of specified persons

##### Requirement to register foreign activity arrangements

65

65.1

A “foreign activity arrangement” is an agreement or arrangement between a
person (“ P ”) and a specified person pursuant to which the specified person
directs P—

65.1.a

to carry out relevant activities in the United Kingdom, or

65.1.b

to arrange for relevant activities to be carried out in the United Kingdom.

65.2

In this section “relevant activities”—

65.2.a

if regulations under subsection  (3)  apply in relation to the specified
person, has the meaning given by the regulations, and

65.2.b

otherwise, means all activities.

65.3

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision about activities
which are relevant activities for the purposes of this section, either in
relation to all specified persons or in relation to such specified persons as
the regulations may provide.

65.4

Where P makes a foreign activity arrangement, P must register the arrangement
with the Secretary of State before the end of the period of 10 days beginning
with the day on which P makes the arrangement.

65.5

P commits an offence if P—

65.5.a

fails to comply with  subsection (4) , and

65.5.b

knows, or having regard to other matters known to them ought reasonably to
know, that the arrangement in question is a foreign activity arrangement.

##### Meaning of “specified person”

66

66.1

“ Specified person ” means—

66.1.a

a foreign power specified by the Secretary of State in regulations;

66.1.b

a person, other than a foreign power, specified by the Secretary of State in
regulations.

66.2

The regulations may specify a person other than a foreign power only if—

66.2.a

the person is not an individual, and

66.2.b

the Secretary of State reasonably believes the person is controlled by a
foreign power.

66.3

Schedule 13  makes provision about when a person is controlled by a foreign
power.

66.4

The Secretary of State may make regulations specifying a foreign power or a
person other than a foreign power only if the Secretary of State considers it
reasonably necessary to do so to protect the safety or interests of the United
Kingdom.

66.5

Regulations specifying a foreign power or a person other than a foreign power
may provide for  section 65 (4)  to apply, with modifications specified in the
regulations, in relation to a foreign activity arrangement made with the
specified person before the regulations come into force.

##### Offence of carrying out etc relevant activities pursuant to unregistered foreign activity arrangement

67

67.1

This section applies where a person (“ P ”) makes a foreign activity
arrangement required to be registered under  section 65 (4) .

67.2

P commits an offence if—

67.2.a

P carries out a relevant activity, or arranges for a relevant activity to be
carried out, in the United Kingdom pursuant to the arrangement,

67.2.b

the arrangement is not registered, and

67.2.c

P knows, or having regard to other matters known to them ought reasonably to
know, that they are acting pursuant to a foreign activity arrangement.

67.3

A person other than P commits an offence if—

67.3.a

the person carries out a relevant activity, or arranges for a relevant
activity to be carried out, in the United Kingdom pursuant to the arrangement,

67.3.b

the arrangement is not registered, and

67.3.c

the person knows, or having regard to other matters known to them ought
reasonably to know, that they are acting pursuant to a foreign activity
arrangement.

67.4

In proceedings for an offence under subsection  (3)  it is a defence to show
that the person—

67.4.a

took all steps reasonably practicable to determine whether the arrangement was
registered, and

67.4.b

reasonably believed that the arrangement was registered.

67.5

A person is taken to have shown a matter mentioned in subsection  (4)  if—

67.5.a

sufficient evidence of the matter is adduced to raise an issue with respect to
it, and

67.5.b

the contrary is not proved beyond reasonable doubt.

67.6

In this section “ relevant activity ” has the same meaning as in  section 65 .

##### Requirement to register relevant activities of specified persons

68

68.1

A specified person who is not a foreign power must not carry out relevant
activities in the United Kingdom unless the activities are registered with the
Secretary of State by the specified person.

68.2

A person who holds office in or under, or is an employee or other member of
staff of, a specified person who is not a foreign power, must not carry out
relevant activities in the United Kingdom in that capacity unless the
activities are registered with the Secretary of State by the specified person.

68.3

A person who holds office in or under, or is an employee or other member of
staff of, a specified person who is a foreign power must not carry out
relevant activities in the United Kingdom in that capacity if or to the extent
that—

68.3.a

the person makes a misrepresentation about their activities or the capacity in
which they act (whether generally or to a particular person), and

68.3.b

the activities are not registered with the Secretary of State by the specified
person.

68.4

In this section “relevant activities”—

68.4.a

if regulations under subsection  (5)  apply in relation to the specified
person, has the meaning given by the regulations, and

68.4.b

otherwise, means all activities.

68.5

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision about activities
which are relevant activities for the purposes of this section, either in
relation to all specified persons or in relation to such specified persons as
the regulations may provide.

68.6

A misrepresentation is a representation that a reasonable person would
consider to be false or misleading in a material way.

68.7

A misrepresentation may be made by making a statement or by any other kind of
conduct (including an omission), and may be express or implied.

68.8

A misrepresentation may in particular include—

68.8.a

a misrepresentation as to the person’s identity or purpose;

68.8.b

presenting information in a way which amounts to a misrepresentation, even if
some or all of the information is true.

68.9

A person who breaches a prohibition in subsection  (1)  or  (2)  commits an
offence.

68.10

A person who breaches a prohibition in subsection  (3)  commits an offence if
the person knows, or having regard to other matters known to them ought
reasonably to know, that paragraph  (a)  of that subsection applies.

68.11

In proceedings for an offence under subsection  (9)  or  (10)  it is a defence
to show that the person—

68.11.a

took all steps reasonably practicable to determine whether the activities were
registered, and

68.11.b

reasonably believed that the activities were registered.

68.12

A person is taken to have shown a matter mentioned in subsection  (11)  if—

68.12.a

sufficient evidence of the matter is adduced to raise an issue with respect to
it, and

68.12.b

the contrary is not proved beyond reasonable doubt.

#### Political influence activities of foreign powers

##### Requirement to register foreign influence arrangements

69

69.1

A “foreign influence arrangement” is an agreement or arrangement between a
person (“ P ”) and a foreign power pursuant to which the foreign power directs
P—

69.1.a

to carry out political influence activities in the United Kingdom, or

69.1.b

to arrange for such activities to be carried out in the United Kingdom.

69.2

Where the foreign power is a specified person, the arrangement is not a
foreign influence arrangement to the extent that it relates to political
influence activities that are relevant activities for the purposes of  section
65 .

69.3

Where P makes a foreign influence arrangement, P must register the arrangement
with the Secretary of State before the end of the period of 28 days beginning
with the day on which P makes the arrangement.

69.4

Subsection (3)  applies in relation to a foreign influence arrangement which
is made before, and which continues to have effect on, the day on which  this
section  comes into force as if, for the words from “28” to the end, there
were substituted  “3 months beginning with the day on which  this section
comes into force.”

69.5

P commits an offence if P—

69.5.a

fails to comply with  subsection (3) , and

69.5.b

knows that the arrangement in question is a foreign influence arrangement.

##### Meaning of “political influence activity”

70

70.1

An activity is a “political influence activity” if—

70.1.a

it is within subsection  (2) , and

70.1.b

the purpose, or one of the purposes, for which it is carried out is the
purpose of influencing a matter or person within subsection  (3) .

70.2

The activities within this subsection are—

70.2.a

making any communication to a person listed in  Schedule 14 ;

70.2.b

making a public communication, except where it is reasonably clear from the
communication that it is made by or at the direction of the foreign power;

70.2.c

distributing money, goods or services to UK persons.

70.3

The matters and persons within this subsection are—

70.3.a

an election or referendum in the United Kingdom,

70.3.b

a decision of—

70.3.b.i

a Minister of the Crown (within the meaning of the Ministers of the Crown Act
1975) or a United Kingdom government department,

70.3.b.ii

a Northern Ireland Minister, the First Minister in Northern Ireland, the
deputy First Minister in Northern Ireland, a person appointed as a junior
Minister under section 19 of the Northern Ireland Act 1998, a Northern Ireland
department or the Executive Committee of the Northern Ireland Assembly,

70.3.b.iii

the Scottish Ministers or the First Minister for Scotland, or

70.3.b.iv

the Welsh Ministers, the First Minister for Wales or the Counsel General to
the Welsh Government,

70.3.c

the proceedings of a UK registered political party, or

70.3.d

a Member of either House of Parliament, the Northern Ireland Assembly, the
Scottish Parliament or Senedd Cymru (acting in that capacity).

70.4

For the purposes of subsection  (2) (b)  a person makes a public communication
if the person—

70.4.a

publishes or disseminates information, a document or other article, or

70.4.b

produces information, a document or other article for publication or
dissemination.

70.5

In  this section —

                                    “ UK person ” has the same meaning as in
section 2 ;
“ UK registered political party ” means a political party registered under
Part 2  of the Political Parties, Elections and Referendums Act 2000.

##### Offence of carrying out etc political influence activities pursuant to unregistered foreign influence arrangement

71

71.1

This section applies where a person (“ P ”) makes a foreign influence
arrangement required to be registered under  section 69 (3) .

71.2

P commits an offence if—

71.2.a

after the end of the registration period P carries out a political influence
activity, or arranges for a political influence activity to be carried out, in
the United Kingdom pursuant to the arrangement,

71.2.b

the arrangement is not registered, and

71.2.c

P knows, or having regard to other matters known to them ought reasonably to
know, that they are acting pursuant to a foreign influence arrangement.

71.3

A person other than P commits an offence if—

71.3.a

after the end of the registration period the person carries out a political
influence activity, or arranges for a political influence activity to be
carried out, in the United Kingdom pursuant to the arrangement,

71.3.b

the arrangement is not registered, and

71.3.c

the person knows, or having regard to other matters known to them ought
reasonably to know, that they are acting pursuant to a foreign influence
arrangement.

71.4

In this section the “ registration period ” means the period before the end of
which P must register the arrangement (see  section 69 (3)  and  (4) ).

71.5

In proceedings for an offence under subsection  (3)  it is a defence to show
that the person—

71.5.a

took all steps reasonably practicable to determine whether the arrangement was
registered, and

71.5.b

reasonably believed that the arrangement was registered.

71.6

A person is taken to have shown a matter mentioned in subsection  (5)  if—

71.6.a

sufficient evidence of the matter is adduced to raise an issue with respect to
it, and

71.6.b

the contrary is not proved beyond reasonable doubt.

##### Requirement to register political influence activities of foreign powers

72

72.1

A person who holds office in or under, or is an employee or other member of
staff of, a foreign power must not carry out political influence activities in
the United Kingdom in that capacity if or to the extent that—

72.1.a

the person makes a misrepresentation about their activities or the capacity in
which they act (whether generally or to a particular person), and

72.1.b

the activities are not registered with the Secretary of State by the foreign
power.

72.2

Where the foreign power is a specified person, the prohibition in  subsection
(1)  does not apply to the extent that the political influence activities are
relevant activities for the purposes of  section 68 .

72.3

A misrepresentation is a representation that a reasonable person would
consider to be false or misleading in a material way.

72.4

A misrepresentation may be made by making a statement or by any other kind of
conduct (including an omission), and may be express or implied.

72.5

A misrepresentation may in particular include—

72.5.a

a misrepresentation as to the person’s identity or purpose;

72.5.b

presenting information in a way which amounts to a misrepresentation, even if
some or all of the information is true.

72.6

A person who breaches a prohibition in subsection  (1)  commits an offence if
the person knows, or having regard to other matters known to them ought
reasonably to know, that paragraph  (a)  of that subsection applies.

72.7

In proceedings for an offence under  subsection (6)  it is a defence to show
that the person—

72.7.a

took all steps reasonably practicable to determine whether the activities were
registered, and

72.7.b

reasonably believed that the activities were registered.

72.8

A person is taken to have shown a matter mentioned in subsection  (7)  if—

72.8.a

sufficient evidence of the matter is adduced to raise an issue with respect to
it, and

72.8.b

the contrary is not proved beyond reasonable doubt.

#### Exemptions

##### Exemptions

73

Schedule 15  makes provision in relation to exemptions.

#### Information

##### Registration information

74

74.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision about the information
a person is required to provide to the Secretary of State when registering—

74.1.a

a foreign activity arrangement under  section 65 ,

74.1.b

a relevant activity under  section 68 ,

74.1.c

a foreign influence arrangement under  section 69 , or

74.1.d

a political influence activity under  section 72 .

74.2

Regulations under  subsection (1)  may, in particular, require the person to
provide information about any arrangements made by the person pursuant to the
arrangement or activity which is required to be registered.

74.3

Regulations under subsection  (1) (c)  may, in particular, require the person
to provide information about any political influence activities carried out,
or arranged to be carried out, during the registration period by any person
pursuant to the arrangement which is required to be registered.

74.4

In subsection  (3)  “ registration period ” has the same meaning as in section
71 .

74.5

Where there is a material change to any information provided to the Secretary
of State under  this section  or  section 75  in relation to a registered
arrangement or a registered activity, the person who registered the
arrangement or activity must inform the Secretary of State of the change
before the end of the period of 14 days beginning with the day on which the
change takes effect.

74.6

The Secretary of State—

74.6.a

may by regulations make provision about the information to be provided to the
Secretary of State under  subsection (5) ,

74.6.b

may issue guidance about what may or may not constitute a material change.

74.7

The provision which may be made by regulations under this section includes
provision about the form in which information is to be provided.

74.8

A person who fails to comply with subsection  (5)  commits an offence if, as a
result of the failure, the information provided to the Secretary of State in
relation to the registered arrangement or registered activity is false,
inaccurate or misleading in a material way.

##### Information notices

75

75.1

The Secretary of State may give an information notice to—

75.1.a

a person who is a party to a foreign activity arrangement registered under
section 65 ;

75.1.b

a person the Secretary of State reasonably believes to be a party to a foreign
activity arrangement which is required to be, but is not, registered under
that section;

75.1.c

a person the Secretary of State reasonably believes to be carrying out
relevant activities, or arranging for relevant activities to be carried out,
in the United Kingdom pursuant to a foreign activity arrangement within
paragraph  (a)  or  (b) ;

75.1.d

a person who has registered relevant activities under  section 68 ;

75.1.e

a person the Secretary of State reasonably believes to be carrying out
relevant activities registered under that section;

75.1.f

a person the Secretary of State reasonably believes to be carrying out
relevant activities in breach of a prohibition in that section.

75.2

The Secretary of State may give an information notice to—

75.2.a

a person who is a party to a foreign influence arrangement registered under
section 69 ;

75.2.b

a person the Secretary of State reasonably believes to be a party to a foreign
influence arrangement which is required to be, but is not, registered under
that section;

75.2.c

a person the Secretary of State reasonably believes to be carrying out
political influence activities, or arranging for political influence
activities to be carried out, in the United Kingdom pursuant to a foreign
influence arrangement within paragraph  (a)  or  (b) ;

75.2.d

a person who has registered political influence activities under  section 72 ;

75.2.e

a person the Secretary of State reasonably believes to be carrying out
political influence activities registered under that section;

75.2.f

a person the Secretary of State reasonably believes to be carrying out
political influence activities in breach of a prohibition in that section.

75.3

An information notice is a notice requiring the person to whom it is given to
supply the information specified in the notice.

75.4

An information notice may only specify information which the Secretary of
State considers may be relevant to an arrangement or activity within
subsection  (1)  or  (2) .

75.5

An information notice must—

75.5.a

specify the form in which the information must be supplied, and

75.5.b

specify the date by which the information must be supplied.

75.6

Where an information notice has been given to a person, the Secretary of State
may cancel it by giving written notice to that effect to the person.

75.7

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision about—

75.7.a

the minimum period between the date on which an information notice is given
and the date specified under  subsection (5) (b) ;

75.7.b

other matters which may be specified in an information notice;

75.7.c

the cancellation of information notices.

75.8

A person commits an offence if, without reasonable excuse, the person fails to
comply with an information notice.

75.9

The Secretary of State may not give an information notice to a foreign power.

##### Confidential material

76

76.1

Nothing in  this Part  is to be taken to require any person to disclose any
information that the person is entitled to refuse to disclose in legal
proceedings on grounds of legal professional privilege (in Scotland,
confidentiality of communications).

76.2

Nothing in this Part is to be taken to require any person to disclose
confidential journalistic material or to identify or confirm a source of
journalistic information.

76.3

In this section—

                                    “ confidential journalistic material ” has
the same meaning as in section 264 of the Investigatory Powers Act 2016;
“ source of journalistic information ” has the same meaning as in section 263
of that Act.

##### Offence of providing false information

77

77.1

A person commits an offence if—

77.1.a

the person provides information to the Secretary of State under  section 74
or  75  in connection with a foreign activity arrangement, and

77.1.b

the information is false, inaccurate or misleading in a material way.

77.2

A person commits an offence if—

77.2.a

the person provides information to the Secretary of State under  section 74
or  75  in connection with a relevant activity which is required to be
registered under  section 68 , and

77.2.b

the information is false, inaccurate or misleading in a material way.

77.3

A person commits an offence if—

77.3.a

the person provides information to the Secretary of State under  section 74
or  75  in connection with a foreign influence arrangement,

77.3.b

the information is false, inaccurate or misleading in a material way, and

77.3.c

the person knows, or having regard to other matters known to them ought
reasonably to know, that the information is false, inaccurate or misleading in
a material way.

77.4

A person commits an offence if—

77.4.a

the person provides information to the Secretary of State under  section 74
or  75  in connection with a political influence activity which is required to
be registered under  section 72 ,

77.4.b

the information is false, inaccurate or misleading in a material way, and

77.4.c

the person knows, or having regard to other matters known to them ought
reasonably to know, that the information is false, inaccurate or misleading in
a material way.

##### Offence of carrying out activities under arrangements tainted by false information

78

78.1

A person commits an offence if—

78.1.a

the person carries out a relevant activity, or arranges for a relevant
activity to be carried out, in the United Kingdom pursuant to a foreign
activity arrangement required to be registered under  section 65 (4) ,

78.1.b

information provided to the Secretary of State under  section 74  or  75  in
connection with the arrangement, whether by the person or by another person,
is false, inaccurate or misleading in a material way, and

78.1.c

the person knows, or having regard to other matters known to them ought
reasonably to know, that the facts are as mentioned in  paragraph (b) .

78.2

A person commits an offence if—

78.2.a

the person carries out a political influence activity, or arranges for a
political influence activity to be carried out, in the United Kingdom pursuant
to a foreign influence arrangement required to be registered under  section 69
(3) ,

78.2.b

information provided to the Secretary of State under  section 74  or  75  in
connection with the arrangement, whether by the person or by another person,
is false, inaccurate or misleading in a material way, and

78.2.c

the person knows, or having regard to other matters known to them ought
reasonably to know, that the facts are as mentioned in  paragraph (b) .

##### Publication and disclosure of information

79

79.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision about—

79.1.a

publication of information provided to the Secretary of State under  section
74  or  75 ;

79.1.b

the disclosure of information provided to the Secretary of State under either
of those sections.

79.2

The power under  subsection (1) (a)  includes in particular power to make
provision about a description of information or material which is not to be
published.

#### Offences: penalties etc

##### Offences: penalties

80

80.1

A person who commits a foreign activity offence is liable—

80.1.a

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 5 years
or to a fine (or both);

80.1.b

on summary conviction in England and Wales, to imprisonment for a term not
exceeding the general limit in a magistrates’ court or to a fine (or both);

80.1.c

on summary conviction in Northern Ireland, to imprisonment for a term not
exceeding 6 months or to a fine not exceeding the statutory maximum (or both);

80.1.d

on summary conviction in Scotland, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 12
months or to a fine not exceeding the statutory maximum (or both).

80.2

“ Foreign activity offence ” means—

80.2.a

an offence under  section 65 (5) ;

80.2.b

an offence under  section 67 ;

80.2.c

an offence under  section 68 (9)  or  (10) ;

80.2.d

an offence under  section 74 (8)  committed in relation to a foreign activity
arrangement registered under  section 65  or a relevant activity registered
under  section 68 ;

80.2.e

an offence under  section 75 (8)  committed in relation to an information
notice given under  section 75 (1) ;

80.2.f

an offence under  section 77 (1)  or  (2) ;

80.2.g

an offence under  section 78 (1) .

80.3

A person who commits a foreign influence offence is liable—

80.3.a

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 2 years
or to a fine (or both);

80.3.b

on summary conviction in England and Wales, to imprisonment for a term not
exceeding the general limit in a magistrates’ court or to a fine (or both);

80.3.c

on summary conviction in Northern Ireland, to imprisonment for a term not
exceeding 6 months or to a fine not exceeding the statutory maximum (or both);

80.3.d

on summary conviction in Scotland, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding 12
months or to a fine not exceeding the statutory maximum (or both).

80.4

“ Foreign influence offence ” means—

80.4.a

an offence under  section 69 (5) ;

80.4.b

an offence under  section 71 ;

80.4.c

an offence under  section 72 (6) ;

80.4.d

an offence under  section 74 (8)  committed in relation to a foreign influence
arrangement registered under  section 69  or a political influence activity
registered under  section 72 ;

80.4.e

an offence under  section 75 (8)  committed in relation to an information
notice given under  section 75 (2) ;

80.4.f

an offence under  section 77 (3)  or  (4) ;

80.4.g

an offence under  section 78 (2) .

##### Offences: supplementary provision

81

81.1

Section  35  (offences by body corporate etc) applies in relation to offences
under  this Part  as it applies in relation to offences under  Part 1 .

81.2

Section  36 (1)  and  (3)  to  (5)  (offences committed outside the United
Kingdom) applies in relation to offences under  this Part  as it applies in
relation to offences under  Part 1 .

81.3

If it is necessary in the interests of national security, a court may exclude
the public from any part of proceedings for an offence under  this Part ,
except for the passing of sentence.

#### Supplementary

##### Annual report

82

82.1

The Secretary of State must, as soon as is practicable after the end of each
relevant period—

82.1.a

prepare a report in relation to that period, and

82.1.b

lay a copy of the report before Parliament.

82.2

The report must provide details of—

82.2.a

the total number of arrangements registered with the Secretary of State under
section 65  or  69 ,

82.2.b

the number of arrangements registered with the Secretary of State under
section 65  or  69  during the relevant period,

82.2.c

the total number of specified persons and foreign powers who have registered
activities with the Secretary of State under  section 68  or  72 ,

82.2.d

the number of specified persons and foreign powers who have registered
activities with the Secretary of State under  section 68  or  72  during the
relevant period,

82.2.e

the number of information notices issued under  section 75  during the
relevant period,

82.2.f

the number of persons charged with an offence under  this Part  during the
relevant period, and

82.2.g

the number of persons convicted of an offence under  this Part  during the
relevant period.

82.3

“ Relevant period ” means—

82.3.a

the period of 12 months beginning with the day on which  this section  comes
into force, and

82.3.b

each subsequent period of 12 months.

##### Interpretation

83

83.1

In this Part—

                                    “ foreign activity arrangement ” has the
meaning given by  section 65 ;
“ foreign influence arrangement ” has the meaning given by  section 69 ;
“ foreign power ” has the same meaning as in Part 1 (see section  32 ),
subject to subsection  (2) ;
“ political influence activity ” has the meaning given by  section 70 ;
“ registered activity ” means an activity registered with the Secretary of
State under  section 68  or  72 ;
“ registered arrangement ” means an arrangement registered with the Secretary
of State under  section 65  or  69 ;
“ specified person ” has the meaning given by  section 66 .

83.2

For the purposes of this Part references in section  32  to a foreign State,
or a foreign country or territory, do not include the Republic of Ireland.

83.3

For the purposes of this Part references to an “arrangement” do not include an
arrangement between a person (“ P ”) and—

83.3.a

a person who holds office in or under, or is an employee or other member of
staff of, P (acting in that capacity), or

83.3.b

a person the Secretary of State reasonably considers to be exercising
functions on behalf of P as if the person were within paragraph  (a) .

### Terrorism

#### Damages in national security proceedings

##### National security proceedings

84

84.1

Sections  85  and  86  apply to proceedings (“national security proceedings”)
before a court which—

84.1.a

are commenced on or after the date this section comes into force,

84.1.b

are brought against the Crown on any grounds (unless they are brought under
section 7(1)(a) of the Human Rights Act 1998), and

84.1.c

relate to national security.

84.2

For the purposes of this section—

84.2.a

proceedings relate to national security where a party to those proceedings
has, at any stage, presented evidence or made submissions to the court
relating to national security;

84.2.b

the circumstances in which evidence or submissions are to be taken to relate
to national security include, in particular, where the evidence or submissions
relate to—

84.2.b.i

the use of investigatory powers or surveillance powers under the Regulation of
Investigatory Powers Act 2000, or the use of similar powers overseas in the
interests of national security;

84.2.b.ii

the activities of the intelligence services in the United Kingdom or overseas,
or the activities of similar services overseas;

84.2.b.iii

investigations or other activities in connection with preventing the
commission of terrorism offences or other involvement in terrorism-related
activity in the United Kingdom or overseas.

##### Duty to consider reduction in damages payable by the Crown

85

85.1

This section applies where—

85.1.a

liability of the Crown to the claimant has been established by the court in
national security proceedings,

85.1.b

the court is permitted to award damages, payable by the Crown, to the claimant
in those proceedings in respect of that liability,

85.1.c

the Crown has made an application to the court for consideration of the
factors mentioned in subsection  (3)  (the “national security factors”), and

85.1.d

the court has not refused the application.

85.2

Where this section applies, the court must, in deciding what remedy (if any)
to award to the claimant in respect of the liability, consider the national
security factors.

85.3

The national security factors are—

85.3.a

whether the claimant has committed wrongdoing that—

85.3.a.i

involves the commission of a terrorism offence or other involvement in
terrorism-related activity, and

85.3.a.ii

has a connection with the conduct of the Crown complained of in the
proceedings, and

85.3.b

if the claimant has committed such wrongdoing—

85.3.b.i

the extent of that wrongdoing and of its connection with the conduct of the
Crown, and

85.3.b.ii

the matters mentioned in  subsection (4) .

85.4

The matters are whether and to what extent—

85.4.a

there was a risk of harm the Crown sought to prevent or limit in carrying out
the conduct complained of in the proceedings;

85.4.b

there was a limitation on the ability of the Crown to prevent the conduct
occurring, including on the basis of—

85.4.b.i

the conduct having occurred overseas, or

85.4.b.ii

the conduct having been carried out in conjunction with a third party.

85.5

Where the court would (but for this subsection) award damages to the claimant
of a particular amount, the court must decide whether, in light of its
consideration of the national security factors, it is appropriate for it to
reduce the amount of damages (including to nil).

85.6

But the court may not decide to reduce damages it would otherwise award to the
claimant under section 8 of the Human Rights Act 1998 (judicial remedies).

85.7

Nothing in this section—

85.7.a

prevents a court from considering the national security factors of its own
motion where this section does not apply;

85.7.b

affects any other power the court may have to reduce damages or to refuse to
award damages, including by reason of—

85.7.b.i

the claimant’s wrongdoing,

85.7.b.ii

the claimant’s failure to mitigate any harm they have suffered, or

85.7.b.iii

the claimant’s contribution to that harm;

85.7.c

affects any existing rule of law otherwise limiting the scope of liability of
the Crown.

##### Section 

86

86.1

An application for consideration of the national security factors may be made
at any time before the final disposal of the national security proceedings
(or, in Scotland, before final judgment in the proceedings within the meaning
given by section 136 of the  Courts Reform (Scotland) Act 2014 (asp 18) ),
including at a time before any liability of the Crown has been established.

86.2

The application must—

86.2.a

set out how the Crown considers the national security factors to apply, and
the Crown’s reasons;

86.2.b

set out the extent to which the Crown considers that damages should be reduced
in light of the national security factors, and the Crown’s reasons;

86.2.c

otherwise be made in accordance with rules of court.

86.3

The court may refuse the application if, in the court’s view, consideration of
the national security factors would—

86.3.a

cause unreasonable delay to the national security proceedings, or

86.3.b

unreasonably prejudice another party to the proceedings.

##### Sections 

87

In sections  84  to  86  and this section—

                  “ claimant ” means a person claiming a remedy of any kind
against the Crown in national security proceedings;
“ court ” includes a tribunal;
“ intelligence service ” means—
the Security Service;
the Secret Intelligence Service;
the Government Communications Headquarters;
“ involvement in terrorism-related activity ” has the same meaning as in the
Terrorism Prevention and Investigation Measures Act 2011 (see section 4 of
that Act);
“ national security factors ” means the factors set out for consideration in
section  85 (3) ;
“ national security proceedings ” has the meaning given by section  84 ;
“ rules of court ” includes tribunal procedure rules;
“ terrorism offence ” means any of the following (whenever committed)—
an offence listed in—
Schedule A1 to the Sentencing Code (terrorism offences: England and Wales), or
Schedule 1A to the Counter-Terrorism Act 2008 (terrorism offences: Scotland
and Northern Ireland);
a service offence as respects which the corresponding civil offence is so
listed; and for this purpose “ service offence ” and “ corresponding civil
offence ” have the same meanings as in the Counter-Terrorism Act 2008 (see
section 95 of that Act);
an offence that—
was abolished on or before the date this section comes into force, and
if committed on or after the date on which it was abolished, would have
constituted an offence referred to in paragraph (a) or (b);
an offence determined to have a terrorist connection under—
section 69 of the Sentencing Code (in the case of an offender sentenced in
England and Wales), including as applied by section 238(6) of the Armed Forces
Act 2006,
section 30 of the Counter-Terrorism Act 2008 (in the case of an offender
sentenced in Northern Ireland, or an offender sentenced in England and Wales
before the Sentencing Code applied), or
section 32 of the Counter-Terrorism Act 2008 (in the case of an offender
sentenced for a service offence before the Sentencing Code applied);
an offence proved to have been aggravated by reason of having a terrorist
connection under section 31 of the Counter-Terrorism Act 2008 (in the case of
an offender sentenced in Scotland).

#### Freezing and forfeiture of damages

##### Damages at risk of being used for the purposes of terrorism

88

Schedule 16  makes provision in relation to damages at risk of being used for
the purposes of terrorism.

#### Legal aid

##### Legal aid for individuals convicted of terrorism offences

89

89.1

The Legal Aid, Sentencing and Punishment of Offenders Act 2012 is amended as
follows.

89.2

In section 9(1) (general cases), at the end insert—

This is subject to section 9A (limits on access to civil legal services for
individuals convicted of terrorism offences).

89.3

After section 9 insert—

########### Limits on access to civil legal services for individuals convicted of terrorism offences

89.3.9A

89.3.9A.1

Civil legal services described in Part 1 of Schedule 1 other than those in
paragraph 12 of Schedule 1 (“general case services”) are only to be available
to an individual convicted of a terrorism offence (an “offender”) under this
Part if—

89.3.9A.1.a

the Director has made a determination under section 9(1)(b) (a “general case
determination”) in relation to the offender (and has not withdrawn the
determination), and

89.3.9A.1.b

the Director determines that one or more of Conditions A to G are met.

89.3.9A.2

Condition A is met where the offender was convicted of the terrorism offence
before 19 February 2001.

89.3.9A.3

Condition B is met where the offender was under the age of 18 on the date they
applied for the general case determination (the “application date”).

89.3.9A.4

Condition C is met where the offender was convicted of the terrorism offence
more than 30 years before the application date.

89.3.9A.5

Condition D is met where the offender was convicted of the terrorism offence—

89.3.9A.5.a

when they were under the age of 18, and

89.3.9A.5.b

more than 15 years before the application date.

89.3.9A.6

Condition E is met where the offender applied for the general case
determination before—

89.3.9A.6.a

the commencement date, or

89.3.9A.6.b

the date on which they were convicted of the terrorism offence.

89.3.9A.7

Condition F is met where the Director has made (and not withdrawn) an
exceptional case determination, within the meaning given by section 10(3), in
relation to the offender and the general case services.

89.3.9A.8

Condition G is met where—

89.3.9A.8.a

the general case services are those described in paragraph 11, 33, 34 or 35 of
Schedule 1 (services in relation to domestic violence and housing), and

89.3.9A.8.b

the offender—

89.3.9A.8.b.i

was or is a victim of domestic violence occurring after the relevant date, or

89.3.9A.8.b.ii

is at risk of being a victim of domestic violence.

89.3.9A.9

In subsection  (8) —

            “ domestic violence ” has the meaning given in paragraph 12(9) of
Schedule 1;
“ relevant date ” means the date five years before the application date.

89.3.9A.10

Regulations may make provision specifying for the purposes of this section
when an individual is deemed to have applied for a general case determination.

89.3.9A.11

In this section, “ terrorism offence ” means any of the following (whenever
committed)—

89.3.9A.11.a

an offence listed in—

89.3.9A.11.a.i

Schedule A1 to the Sentencing Code (terrorism offences: England and Wales), or

89.3.9A.11.a.ii

Schedule 1A to the Counter-Terrorism Act 2008 (terrorism offences: Scotland
and Northern Ireland);

89.3.9A.11.b

a service offence as respects which the corresponding civil offence is so
listed;

89.3.9A.11.c

an offence that—

89.3.9A.11.c.i

was abolished on or before the commencement date, and

89.3.9A.11.c.ii

if committed on or after the date on which it was abolished, would have
constituted an offence referred to in paragraph  (a)  or  (b) ;

89.3.9A.11.d

an offence determined to have a terrorist connection under—

89.3.9A.11.d.i

section 69 of the Sentencing Code (in the case of an offender sentenced in
England and Wales), including as applied by section 238(6) of the Armed Forces
Act 2006,

89.3.9A.11.d.ii

section 30 of the Counter-Terrorism Act 2008 (in the case of an offender
sentenced in Northern Ireland, or an offender sentenced in England and Wales
before the Sentencing Code applied), or

89.3.9A.11.d.iii

section 32 of the Counter-Terrorism Act 2008 (in the case of an offender
sentenced for a service offence before the Sentencing Code applied);

89.3.9A.11.e

an offence proved to have been aggravated by reason of having a terrorist
connection under section 31 of the Counter-Terrorism Act 2008 (in the case of
an offender sentenced in Scotland).

89.3.9A.12

Where an offender has been convicted of more than one terrorism offence, “the
terrorism offence” in this section means the terrorism offence the offender
has most recently been convicted of.

89.3.9A.13

In this section—

            “ commencement date ” means the date on which section  89  of the
National Security Act 2023 comes into force;
“ service offence ” and “ corresponding civil offence ” have the same meanings
as in the Counter-Terrorism Act 2008 (see section 95 of that Act).

89.3.9A.14

Nothing in this section affects the Director’s ability to make determinations
under section 10 (exceptional cases).

89.4

In section 12 (determinations)—

89.4.a

in subsection (2), after “9” insert  “, 9A” ;

89.4.b

in subsection (5), after “9” insert  “, 9A” .

##### Legal aid for individuals convicted of terrorism offences: data sharing

90

In the Legal Aid, Sentencing and Punishment of Offenders Act 2012, after
section 9A (as inserted by section  89 ) insert—

######### Information relating to convictions for terrorism offences

90.9B

90.9B.1

The Director may make an information request to a competent authority.

90.9B.2

An information request under this section may be made only for the purpose of
identifying—

90.9B.2.a

whether an individual who has applied for a determination under section 9 has
been convicted of a terrorism offence, and

90.9B.2.b

if the individual has been so convicted, details relating to that conviction.

90.9B.3

An information request under this section may in particular request the
disclosure of any of the following—

90.9B.3.a

a relevant individual’s full name and any previous names;

90.9B.3.b

a relevant individual’s address and any previous addresses;

90.9B.3.c

a relevant individual’s date of birth;

90.9B.3.d

a relevant individual’s national insurance number;

90.9B.3.e

a number identifying a relevant individual in a system maintained by a body
established in accordance with a collaboration agreement under section 22A of
the Police Act 1996;

90.9B.3.f

a number identifying a relevant individual in a system maintained by the
Secretary of State for the management of offenders;

90.9B.3.g

any convictions of a relevant individual;

90.9B.3.h

any details relating to those convictions, including the date of conviction
and any sentence imposed.

90.9B.4

A competent authority may disclose to the Director information specified in an
information request made under this section.

90.9B.5

The Director may, for the purposes of deciding whether general case services
are to be available to an individual under this Part, process any personal
data in respect of a relevant individual disclosed by a competent authority to
the Director under this section.

90.9B.6

This section does not authorise the disclosure or processing of information if
the disclosure or processing would contravene the data protection legislation
(but, in determining whether a disclosure or processing would do so, the
powers conferred by this section are to be taken into account).

90.9B.7

In this section—

                                                                        “
competent authority ” has the same meaning as in section 30 of the Data
Protection Act 2018;
“ general case services ” and “ terrorism offence ” have the same meanings as
in section 9A;
“ personal data ”, “ processing ” and “ the data protection legislation ” have
the same meanings as in section 3 of the Data Protection Act 2018;
“ relevant individual ” means—
an individual who has applied for a determination under section 9, or
an individual who has been convicted of a terrorism offence.

#### General provisions

##### Minor and consequential amendments

94

Schedule 18  makes minor and consequential amendments.

##### Power to make consequential amendments

95

95.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision that is consequential
on any provision of this Act.

95.2

The provision that may be made by regulations under  subsection (1)  includes
provision amending primary legislation.

95.3

“ Primary legislation ” means—

95.3.a

an Act of Parliament,

95.3.b

a Measure or Act of Senedd Cymru,

95.3.c

an Act of the Scottish Parliament,

95.3.d

Northern Ireland legislation, or

95.3.e

retained direct principal EU legislation,

whenever passed or made.

##### Regulations

96

96.1

A power to make regulations under any provision of this Act includes power to
make—

96.1.a

consequential, supplementary, incidental, transitional or saving provision;

96.1.b

different provision for different purposes or different areas.

96.2

Subsection (1)  does not apply to regulations under  section 100  or  101 .

96.3

Regulations under this Act are to be made by statutory instrument.

96.4

Regulations under this Act are subject to annulment in pursuance of a
resolution of either House of Parliament, except—

96.4.a

regulations under  section 100  or  101 ;

96.4.b

regulations to which  subsection (6)  applies;

96.4.c

regulations under paragraph  46  of Schedule  6 .

96.5

A statutory instrument containing (whether alone or with other provision)
regulations to which  subsection (6)  applies may not be made unless a draft
of the instrument has been laid before, and approved by a resolution of, each
House of Parliament.

96.6

This subsection  applies to—

96.6.a

regulations under  section 65 (3) ;

96.6.b

regulations under section  66  specifying a foreign power, or a person other
than a foreign power, who is not specified immediately before the regulations
are made;

96.6.c

regulations under  section 68 (5) ;

96.6.d

regulations under  section 79 (1) (a) ;

96.6.e

regulations under  section 95  which contain provision within  section 95 (2)
;

96.6.f

regulations under paragraph  3 (2) (b)  of Schedule  6 ;

96.6.g

regulations under paragraph  4 (3)  of Schedule  6 ;

96.6.h

regulations under paragraph  15  of  Schedule 13 ;

96.6.i

regulations under paragraph  27  of  Schedule 14 ;

96.6.j

regulations under  paragraph 8  of  Schedule 15 .

96.7

A statutory instrument containing regulations under paragraph  46  of Schedule
6  must be laid before Parliament as soon as practicable after being made.

96.8

Regulations contained in a statutory instrument laid before Parliament under
subsection (7)  cease to have effect at the end of the period of 20 days
beginning with the day on which the instrument is made unless, during that
period, the instrument is approved by a resolution of each House of
Parliament.

96.9

In calculating the period of 20 days no account is to be taken of any whole
days that fall within a period during which—

96.9.a

Parliament is dissolved or prorogued, or

96.9.b

either House of Parliament is adjourned for more than four days.

96.10

Subsections (8)  and  (9)  do not apply to regulations under paragraph  46  of
Schedule  6  which revoke regulations under that paragraph.

96.11

If a draft of a statutory instrument containing regulations under  section 65
,  66  or  68  would, apart from this subsection, be treated for the purposes
of the standing orders of either House of Parliament as a hybrid instrument,
it is to proceed in that House as if it were not such an instrument.

##### Crown application

97

97.1

This Act binds the Crown, subject as follows.

97.2

No contravention by the Crown of a provision of this Act makes the Crown
criminally liable.

97.3

Subsection (2)  does not affect the criminal liability of persons in the
service of the Crown.

97.4

An amendment or repeal made by this Act binds the Crown to the same extent as
the provision amended or repealed.

##### Extent in the United Kingdom

98

98.1

This Act extends to England and Wales, Scotland and Northern Ireland, subject
to—

98.1.a

subsection (2) , and

98.1.b

section 99 .

98.2

An amendment or repeal made by this Act has the same extent in the United
Kingdom as the provision to which it relates.

##### Extent outside the United Kingdom

99

99.1

Section  22  extends to—

99.1.a

the Isle of Man, and

99.1.b

the British Overseas Territories, except Gibraltar.

99.2

His Majesty may by Order in Council provide for any provision of this Act
other than section  22  to extend (with or without modifications) to the
Sovereign Base Areas of Akrotiri and Dhekelia.

99.3

An Order in Council under subsection  (2)  may make consequential,
supplementary, incidental, transitional or saving provision.

99.4

The power under section 384(1) of the Armed Forces Act 2006 may be exercised
so as to extend to any of the Channel Islands (with or without modifications)
the amendment of section 238 of the Armed Forces Act 2006 made by section  22
.

99.5

The power under section 384(2) of the Armed Forces Act 2006 may be exercised
so as to modify section 238 of the Armed Forces Act 2006, as amended by
section  22 , as it extends to the Isle of Man or a British overseas territory
other than Gibraltar.

99.6

The power under section 15(3) of the Official Secrets Act 1989 may be
exercised so as to extend to any of the Channel Islands, the Isle of Man or a
British Overseas Territory any amendment or repeal made by this Act of any
provision of that Act.

99.7

The power under section 415 of the Sentencing Act 2020 may be exercised so as
to extend to any of the Channel Islands or the Isle of Man (with or without
modifications) any amendment or repeal made by this Act of any provision of
that Act.

##### Commencement

100

100.1

This Act comes into force on such day as the Secretary of State may by
regulations appoint, subject to  subsection (2) .

100.2

Sections 95  to  102  come into force on the day on which this Act is passed.

100.3

A power to make regulations under  this section  includes power to appoint
different days for different purposes or areas.

##### Transitional and saving provision

101

101.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations make transitional or saving
provision in connection with the coming into force of any provision of this
Act.

101.2

A power to make regulations under this section includes power to make
different provision for different purposes or areas.

##### Short title

102

This Act may be cited as the National Security Act 2023.

Powers of entry, search and seizure

Section 23

##### England and Wales and Northern Ireland

###### Introductory

1

1.1

This Part  of  this Schedule  applies in England and Wales and in Northern
Ireland.

1.2

In  this Part  of  this Schedule  “ relevant act ” means—

1.2.a

an offence under  this Part  of this Act, other than an offence under—

1.2.a.i

section  5  (unauthorised entry to a prohibited place);

1.2.a.ii

section  6  (prohibited place: failure to comply with order of constable);

1.2.a.iii

section  11  (cordoned area: failure to comply with order of constable);

1.2.a.iv

this Schedule ;

1.2.a.v

Schedule  3  (disclosure orders);

1.2.a.vi

Schedule  4  (customer information orders);

1.2.b

an act or threat within section  33 (3) (b)  or  (c) .

###### Material other than confidential material: search, seizure and retention

2

2.1

A constable may make an application for the issue of a warrant under  this
paragraph —

2.1.a

in England and Wales, to a justice of the peace;

2.1.b

in Northern Ireland, to a lay magistrate.

2.2

The justice of the peace or lay magistrate may grant the application if
satisfied that—

2.2.a

conditions 1 and 2 are met, and

2.2.b

in the case of an application for an all premises warrant, condition 3 is met.

2.3

Condition 1 is that there are reasonable grounds for suspecting that a
relevant act has been, or is about to be, committed.

2.4

Condition 2 is that there are reasonable grounds for suspecting that there is
on the relevant premises material which—

2.4.a

is likely to be evidence that a relevant act has been, or is about to be,
committed, and

2.4.b

does not consist of or include confidential material.

2.5

Condition 3 is that it is not reasonably practicable to specify in the
application all the premises which the person specified in the application
occupies or controls and which might need to be searched.

2.6

A warrant under  this paragraph  is a warrant authorising any constable—

2.6.a

to enter the relevant premises,

2.6.b

to search the relevant premises and any person found there, and

2.6.c

to seize and retain any material found on a search under  paragraph (b)  which
is likely to be evidence that a relevant act has been, or is about to be,
committed.

2.7

A warrant under  this paragraph  does not authorise—

2.7.a

the seizure and retention of confidential material, or

2.7.b

a constable to require a person to remove any clothing in public except for
headgear, footwear, an outer coat or jacket and gloves.

2.8

In  this paragraph  the “relevant premises” are—

2.8.a

one or more sets of premises specified in the application (in which case the
application is for a “specific premises warrant”), or

2.8.b

any premises occupied or controlled by a person specified in the application,
including such sets of premises as are so specified (in which case the
application is for an “all premises warrant”).

###### Confidential material: production orders

3

3.1

A constable may apply to a judge for an order under  this paragraph .

3.2

The judge may grant the application if satisfied that conditions 1 to 4 are
met.

3.3

Condition 1 is that there are reasonable grounds for suspecting that a
relevant act has been, or is about to be, committed.

3.4

Condition 2 is that there are reasonable grounds for suspecting that a person
specified in the application has in their possession, custody or control
material which—

3.4.a

is likely to be evidence that a relevant act has been, or is about to be,
committed,

3.4.b

consists of or includes confidential material, and

3.4.c

does not include items subject to legal privilege.

3.5

Condition 3 is that there are reasonable grounds for believing that the
material is likely to be of substantial value, whether by itself or with other
material, to an investigation into whether a relevant act has been, or is
about to be, committed.

3.6

Condition 4 is that there are reasonable grounds for believing that it is in
the public interest that the material should be produced or access to it
should be given having regard to—

3.6.a

the benefit likely to accrue to the investigation if the material is obtained,
and

3.6.b

the circumstances under which the person concerned has any of the material in
their possession, custody or control.

3.7

An order under  this paragraph  is an order that the person specified in the
application must do any of the following—

3.7.a

produce to a constable within a specified period for seizure and retention any
material which the person has in their possession, custody or control and to
which the application relates;

3.7.b

give a constable access to any material of the kind mentioned in  paragraph
(a)  within a specified period;

3.7.c

state to the best of the person’s knowledge and belief the location of the
material to which the application relates if it is not in, and will not come
into, the person’s possession, custody or control within the period specified
under  paragraph (a)  or  (b) .

3.8

The specified period is to be the period of 7 days beginning with the date of
the order, unless it appears to the judge that a different period would be
appropriate in the particular circumstances of the application.

4

4.1

A constable may apply to a judge for an order under  this paragraph .

4.2

The judge may grant the application if satisfied that conditions 1 to 5 are
met.

4.3

Condition 1 is that there are reasonable grounds for suspecting that a
relevant act has been, or is about to be, committed.

4.4

Condition 2 is that there are reasonable grounds for suspecting that, within
the period of 28 days beginning with the date of the order, there is likely to
come into existence material which—

4.4.a

is evidence that a relevant act has been, or is about to be, committed,

4.4.b

consists of or includes confidential material, and

4.4.c

does not include items subject to legal privilege.

4.5

Condition 3 is that there are reasonable grounds for suspecting that a person
specified in the application is likely within that period to have in their
possession, custody or control any of the material to which the application
relates.

4.6

Condition 4 is that there are reasonable grounds for believing that the
