specified work or work of a specified description, or

10.2.a.ii

specified studies or studies of a specified description;

10.2.b

a requirement to give notice to the Secretary of State before carrying out any
work or studies;

10.2.c

a requirement to comply with any other specified conditions in connection with
any work or studies.

10.3

In  this paragraph —

                                             “ studies ” includes any course
of education or training;
“ work ” includes any business or occupation (whether paid or unpaid).

###### Reporting measure

11

11.1

The Secretary of State may impose a requirement for the individual—

11.1.a

to report to such a police station, at such times and in such manner, as the
Secretary of State may by notice require, and

11.1.b

to comply with any directions given by a constable in relation to such
reporting.

11.2

Such a notice may, in particular, provide that a requirement to report to a
police station is not to apply if conditions specified in the notice are met.

###### Polygraph measure

12

12.1

The Secretary of State may impose a requirement for the individual—

12.1.a

to participate in polygraph sessions conducted with a view to—

12.1.a.i

monitoring the individual’s compliance with other specified measures;

12.1.a.ii

assessing whether any variation of the specified measures is necessary for
purposes connected with preventing or restricting the individual’s involvement
in foreign power threat activity,

12.1.b

to participate in those polygraph sessions at such times as may be specified
in instructions given by the Secretary of State, and

12.1.c

while participating in a polygraph session, to comply with instructions given
to the individual by the polygraph operator.

12.2

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision relating to the
conduct of polygraph sessions, which may include in particular—

12.2.a

provision requiring polygraph operators to be persons who satisfy such
requirements as to qualifications, experience and other matters as are
specified in the regulations;

12.2.b

provision about the keeping of records of polygraph sessions;

12.2.c

provision about the preparation of reports on the results of polygraph
sessions.

12.3

The measurement and recording of the physiological reactions of an individual
while being questioned in the course of a polygraph examination must be done
by means of equipment of a type approved by the Secretary of State.

12.4

The following may not be used in evidence against the individual in any
proceedings for an offence—

12.4.a

any statement made by the individual while participating in a polygraph
session;

12.4.b

any physiological reaction of the individual while being questioned in the
course of a polygraph examination.

12.5

In  this paragraph —

                                             “ polygraph examination ” means a
procedure in which—
the polygraph operator questions the individual,
the questions and the individual’s answers are recorded, and
physiological reactions of the individual while being questioned are measured
and recorded;
“ polygraph operator ” means the person conducting a polygraph session;
“ polygraph session ” means a session during which the polygraph operator—
conducts one or more polygraph examinations of the individual, and
interviews the individual in preparation for, or otherwise in connection with,
any such examination.

###### Appointments measure

13

13.1

The Secretary of State may impose a requirement for the individual—

13.1.a

to attend appointments with specified persons or persons of specified
descriptions, and

13.1.b

to comply with any reasonable directions given by the Secretary of State that
relate to matters about which the individual is required to attend an
appointment.

13.2

A requirement under  sub-paragraph (1) (a)  is a requirement to attend
appointments—

13.2.a

at specified times and places, or

13.2.b

at times and places notified to the individual by persons referred to in that
sub-paragraph.

###### Photography measure

14

The Secretary of State may impose a requirement for the individual to allow
photographs to be taken of the individual at such locations and at such times
as the Secretary of State may by notice require.

###### Monitoring measure

15

15.1

The Secretary of State may impose requirements for the individual to co-
operate with specified arrangements for enabling the individual’s movements,
communications or other activities to be monitored by electronic or other
means.

15.2

The Secretary of State may, in particular, impose any of the following
requirements for co-operation with the specified arrangements—

15.2.a

a requirement to submit to procedures required by the arrangements;

15.2.b

a requirement to wear or otherwise use apparatus approved by or in accordance
with the arrangements;

15.2.c

a requirement to maintain such apparatus in a specified manner;

15.2.d

a requirement to comply with directions given by persons carrying out
functions for the purposes of the arrangements.

15.3

Directions under  sub-paragraph (2) (d)  may include directions requiring the
individual to grant access to the individual’s residence for the purpose of
the inspection or modification of any apparatus used or maintained under the
arrangements.

###### Provision of residence information measure

16

16.1

The Secretary of State may impose a requirement for the individual to disclose
to the Secretary of State—

16.1.a

the address of the individual’s residence;

16.1.b

if the individual resides at multiple occupancy premises, such details as may
be specified concerning where, in the premises, the individual’s residence is
located;

16.1.c

such details as may be specified in relation to any change (or anticipated
change) in the matters referred to in paragraphs  (a)  and  (b) .

16.2

The Secretary of State may impose a requirement for the individual to comply
with any other specified conditions in connection with the disclosure of
information within  sub-paragraph (1) .

16.3

“Multiple occupancy premises” are premises at which two or more individuals
who are not members of the same household reside.

##### Permission and notices

###### Permission

17

17.1

Any application by an individual for permission must be made in writing.

17.2

The Secretary of State may by notice specify—

17.2.a

the information to be supplied on an application, and

17.2.b

the time by which the application is to be made.

17.3

A notice under  sub-paragraph (2)  may make different provision for different
measures.

17.4

The Secretary of State may by notice request the provision, within such period
of time as the notice may specify, of further information from the individual
in connection with an application received under  sub-paragraph (1) .

17.5

The Secretary of State is not required to consider an application further
unless any information requested under  sub-paragraph (4)  is provided in
accordance with the notice mentioned in that sub-paragraph.

17.6

Permission on an application is granted by the Secretary of State giving
notice to the individual.

17.7

Permission may be granted subject to such conditions as the Secretary of State
may by notice specify.

17.8

In  this paragraph  “ permission ” means permission in connection with a
requirement or restriction imposed under  Part 1  of  this Schedule .

###### Notices

18

18.1

This paragraph  applies for the purposes of any notice given by the individual
to the Secretary of State in connection with measures imposed under  Part 1
of  this Schedule  (“a  Schedule 7  notice”).

18.2

The Secretary of State may by notice specify—

18.2.a

the information to be supplied in a  Schedule 7  notice, and

18.2.b

the time by which a  Schedule 7  notice is to be given.

18.3

A notice under  sub-paragraph (2)  may make different provision for different
measures.

18.4

The Secretary of State may by notice request the provision, within such period
of time as the notice may specify, of further information from the individual
in connection with a  Schedule 7  notice received from the individual.

18.5

A requirement on the individual to give a  Schedule 7  notice is not complied
with unless and until the individual has received notice from the Secretary of
State—

18.5.a

that the  Schedule 7  notice has been received, and

18.5.b

that no (or no further) information is required under  sub-paragraph (4)  in
relation to the  Schedule 7  notice.

###### Power of Secretary of State to vary or revoke notices

19

The Secretary of State may vary or revoke a notice given by the Secretary of
State under  this Schedule .

                 Urgent cases: reference to the court etc

Section 43

##### Application

1

This Schedule  applies if the Secretary of State—

1.a

makes the relevant decisions in relation to an individual, and

1.b

imposes measures on the individual.

##### Statement of urgency

2

The  Part 2  notice must include a statement that the Secretary of State
reasonably considers that the urgency of the case requires measures to be
imposed without obtaining the permission of the court under  section 42 .

##### Reference to court

3

3.1

Immediately after serving the  Part 2  notice, the Secretary of State must
refer to the court the imposition of the measures on the individual.

3.2

The function of the court on the reference is to consider whether the relevant
decisions of the Secretary of State were obviously flawed.

3.3

The court’s consideration of the reference must begin within the period of 7
days beginning with the day on which the  Part 2  notice is served on the
individual.

3.4

The court may consider the reference—

3.4.a

in the absence of the individual,

3.4.b

without the individual having been notified of the reference, and

3.4.c

without the individual having been given an opportunity (if the individual was
aware of the reference) of making any representations to the court.

3.5

But that does not limit the matters about which rules of court may be made.

##### Decision by court

4

4.1

In a case where the court determines that a decision of the Secretary of State
that condition A, condition B or condition C is met is obviously flawed, the
court must quash the  Part 2  notice.

4.2

In a case where the court determines that a decision of the Secretary of State
that condition D is met is obviously flawed, the court must quash those of the
measures which it determines that decision relates to.

4.3

If  sub-paragraph (1)  does not apply, the court must confirm the  Part 2
notice (subject to any quashing of measures under  sub-paragraph (2) ).

4.4

If the court determines that the Secretary of State’s decision that the
urgency condition is met is obviously flawed, the court must make a
declaration of that determination (whether it quashes or confirms the  Part 2
notice under the preceding provisions of  this paragraph ).

##### Procedures on reference

5

5.1

In determining a reference under  paragraph 3 , the court must apply the
principles applicable on an application for judicial review.

5.2

The court must ensure that the individual is notified of the court's decision
on a reference under  paragraph 3 .

##### Interpretation

6

6.1

References in  this Schedule  to the urgency condition being met are
references to condition E being met by virtue of  section 40 (5) (b)  (urgency
of the case requires measures to be imposed without obtaining the permission
of the court).

6.2

In  this Schedule  “ relevant decisions ” means the decisions that the
following conditions are met—

6.2.a

condition A;

6.2.b

condition B;

6.2.c

condition C;

6.2.d

condition D;

6.2.e

the urgency condition.

                 Appeals against convictions

Section 51

1

An individual who has been convicted of an offence under section  56 (1)  may
appeal against the conviction if—

1.a

a  Part 2  notice, the extension of a  Part 2  notice, or the revival of a
Part 2  notice is quashed, or measures specified in a  Part 2  notice are
quashed, and

1.b

the individual could not have been convicted had the quashing occurred before
the proceedings for the offence were brought.

2

An appeal under  this Schedule  is to be made—

2.a

in the case of a conviction on indictment in England and Wales or Northern
Ireland, to the Court of Appeal,

2.b

in the case of a conviction on indictment in Scotland, to the High Court of
Justiciary,

2.c

in the case of a summary conviction in England and Wales, to the Crown Court,

2.d

in the case of a summary conviction in Scotland, to the Sheriff Appeal Court,
or

2.e

in the case of a summary conviction in Northern Ireland, to the county court.

3

3.1

The right of appeal under  this Schedule  does not arise until there is no
further possibility of an appeal against—

3.1.a

the decision to quash the notice, extension, revival or measures, or

3.1.b

any decision on an appeal made against that decision.

3.2

In determining whether there is no further possibility of an appeal against a
decision of the kind mentioned in  sub-paragraph (1) , any power to extend the
time for giving notice of application for leave to appeal, or for applying for
leave to appeal, must be ignored.

4

4.1

On an appeal under  this Schedule  to any court, that court must allow the
appeal and quash the conviction.

4.2

An appeal under  this Schedule  to the Court of Appeal against a conviction on
indictment in England and Wales or Northern Ireland—

4.2.a

may be brought irrespective of whether the appellant has previously appealed
against the conviction,

4.2.b

may not be brought after the end of the period of 28 days beginning with the
day on which the right of appeal arises by virtue of  paragraph 3 , and

4.2.c

is to be treated as an appeal under section 1 of the Criminal Appeal Act 1968
or, in Northern Ireland, under section 1 of the Criminal Appeal (Northern
Ireland) Act 1980, but does not require leave in either case.

4.3

An appeal under  this Schedule  to the High Court of Justiciary against a
conviction on indictment in Scotland—

4.3.a

may be brought irrespective of whether the appellant has previously appealed
against the conviction,

4.3.b

may not be brought after the end of the period of 28 days beginning with the
day on which the right of appeal arises by virtue of  paragraph 3 , and

4.3.c

is to be treated as an appeal under section 106 of the Criminal Procedure
(Scotland) Act 1995 for which leave has been granted.

4.4

An appeal under  this Schedule  to the Crown Court against a summary
conviction in England and Wales—

4.4.a

may be brought irrespective of whether the appellant pleaded guilty,

4.4.b

may be brought irrespective of whether the appellant has previously appealed
against the conviction or made an application in respect of the conviction
under section 111 of the Magistrates’ Courts Act 1980 (case stated),

4.4.c

may not be brought after the end of the period of 21 days beginning with the
day on which the right of appeal arises by virtue of  paragraph 3 , and

4.4.d

is to be treated as an appeal under section 108(1)(b) of the Magistrates'
Courts Act 1980.

4.5

An appeal under  this Schedule  to the Sheriff Appeal Court against a summary
conviction in Scotland—

4.5.a

may be brought irrespective of whether the appellant pleaded guilty,

4.5.b

may be brought irrespective of whether the appellant has previously appealed
against the conviction,

4.5.c

may not be brought after the end of the period of two weeks beginning with the
day on which the right of appeal arises by virtue of  paragraph 3 ,

4.5.d

is to be by note of appeal, which shall state the ground of appeal,

4.5.e

is to be treated as an appeal for which leave has been granted under Part 10
of the Criminal Procedure (Scotland) Act 1995, and

4.5.f

must be in accordance with such procedure as the High Court of Justiciary may,
by Act of Adjournal, determine.

4.6

An appeal under  this Schedule  to the county court against a summary
conviction in Northern Ireland—

4.6.a

may be brought irrespective of whether the appellant pleaded guilty,

4.6.b

may be brought irrespective of whether the appellant has previously appealed
against the conviction or made an application in respect of the conviction
under Article 146 of the Magistrates' Courts (Northern Ireland) Order 1981 (
S.I. 1981/1675 (N.I. 26) ) (case stated),

4.6.c

may not be brought after the end of the period of 21 days beginning with the
day on which the right of appeal arises by virtue of  paragraph 3 , and

4.6.d

is to be treated as an appeal under Article 140(1)(b) of the Magistrates’
Courts (Northern Ireland) Order 1981 ( S.I. 1981/1675 (N.I. 26) ).

Proceedings relating to prevention and investigation measures

Section 54

##### Introductory

1

In  this Schedule —

“ appeal proceedings ” means proceedings in the Court of Appeal or the Inner
House of the Court of Session on an appeal relating to relevant proceedings; “
the relevant court ” means— in relation to relevant proceedings, the court; in
relation to appeal proceedings, the Court of Appeal or the Inner House of the
Court of Session; “ rules of court ” means rules for regulating the practice
and procedure to be followed in the court, the Court of Appeal or the Inner
House of the Court of Session.

##### Rules of court: general provision

2

2.1

A person making rules of court relating to relevant proceedings or appeal
proceedings must have regard to the need to secure the following—

2.1.a

that the decisions that are the subject of the proceedings are properly
reviewed, and

2.1.b

that disclosures of information are not made where they would be contrary to
the public interest.

2.2

Rules of court relating to relevant proceedings or appeal proceedings may make
provision—

2.2.a

about the mode of proof and about evidence in the proceedings;

2.2.b

enabling or requiring the proceedings to be determined without a hearing;

2.2.c

about legal representation in the proceedings;

2.2.d

enabling the proceedings to take place without full particulars of the reasons
for the decisions to which the proceedings relate being given to a party to
the proceedings (or to any legal representative of that party);

2.2.e

enabling the relevant court to conduct proceedings in the absence of any
person, including a party to the proceedings (or any legal representative of
that party);

2.2.f

about the functions of a person appointed as a special advocate (see
paragraph 10 );

2.2.g

enabling the court to give a party to the proceedings a summary of evidence
taken in the party’s absence.

2.3

In  this paragraph —

2.3.a

references to a party to the proceedings do not include the Secretary of
State;

2.3.b

references to a party’s legal representative do not include a person appointed
as a special advocate.

2.4

Nothing in  this paragraph  is to be read as restricting the power to make
rules of court or the matters to be taken into account when doing so.

##### Rules of court: disclosure

3

3.1

Rules of court relating to relevant proceedings or appeal proceedings must
secure that the Secretary of State is required to disclose—

3.1.a

material on which the Secretary of State relies,

3.1.b

material which adversely affects the Secretary of State’s case, and

3.1.c

material which supports the case of another party to the proceedings.

3.2

This paragraph  is subject to  paragraph 4 .

4

4.1

Rules of court relating to relevant proceedings or appeal proceedings must
secure—

4.1.a

that the Secretary of State has the opportunity to make an application to the
relevant court for permission not to disclose material otherwise than to the
relevant court and any person appointed as a special advocate;

4.1.b

that such an application is always considered in the absence of every party to
the proceedings (and every party’s legal representative);

4.1.c

that the relevant court is required to give permission for material not to be
disclosed if it considers that the disclosure of the material would be
contrary to the public interest;

4.1.d

that, if permission is given by the relevant court not to disclose material,
it must consider requiring the Secretary of State to provide a summary of the
material to every party to the proceedings (and every party’s legal
representative);

4.1.e

that the relevant court is required to ensure that such a summary does not
contain material the disclosure of which would be contrary to the public
interest.

4.2

Rules of court relating to relevant proceedings or appeal proceedings must
secure that provision to the effect mentioned in  sub-paragraph (3)  applies
in cases where the Secretary of State—

4.2.a

does not receive the permission of the relevant court to withhold material,
but elects not to disclose it, or

4.2.b

is required to provide a party to the proceedings with a summary of material
that is withheld, but elects not to provide the summary.

4.3

The relevant court must be authorised—

4.3.a

if it considers that the material or anything that is required to be
summarised might adversely affect the Secretary of State’s case or support the
case of a party to the proceedings, to direct that the Secretary of State—

4.3.a.i

is not to rely on such points in the Secretary of State’s case, or

4.3.a.ii

is to make such concessions or take such other steps as the court may specify,
or

4.3.b

in any other case, to ensure that the Secretary of State does not rely on the
material or (as the case may be) on that which is required to be summarised.

4.4

In  this paragraph —

4.4.a

references to a party to the proceedings do not include the Secretary of
State;

4.4.b

references to a party’s legal representative do not include a person appointed
as a special advocate.

##### Article 6 rights

5

5.1

Nothing in  paragraphs 2  to  4 , or in rules of court made under any of those
paragraphs, is to be read as requiring the relevant court to act in a manner
inconsistent with Article  6  of the Human Rights Convention.

5.2

The “ Human Rights Convention ” means the Convention within the meaning of the
Human Rights Act 1998 (see section 21(1) of that Act).

##### Rules of court: anonymity

6

6.1

Rules of court relating to relevant proceedings or appeal proceedings may make
provision for—

6.1.a

the making by the Secretary of State or the relevant individual of an
application to the court for an order requiring anonymity for that individual,
and

6.1.b

the making by the court, on such an application, of an order requiring such
anonymity,

and the provision made by the rules may allow the application and the order to
be made irrespective of whether any other relevant proceedings have been begun
in the court.

6.2

Rules of court may provide for the Court of Appeal or the Inner House of the
Court of Session to make an order in connection with any appeal proceedings
requiring anonymity for the relevant individual.

6.3

In  sub-paragraphs (1)  and  (2)  the references, in relation to a court, to
an order requiring anonymity for the relevant individual are references to an
order by that court which imposes such prohibition or restriction as it thinks
fit on the disclosure—

6.3.a

by such persons as the court specifies or describes, or

6.3.b

by persons generally,

of the identity of the relevant individual or of any information that would
tend to identify the relevant individual.

6.4

In  this paragraph  “ relevant individual ” means an individual on whom the
Secretary of State is proposing to impose, or has imposed, measures.

##### Initial exercise of rule-making powers by Lord Chancellor

7

7.1

The first time that rules of court are made in exercise of the powers
conferred by  this Schedule  in relation to proceedings in England and Wales
or in Northern Ireland, the rules may be made by the Lord Chancellor instead
of by the person who would otherwise make them.

7.2

Before making rules of court under  sub-paragraph (1) , the Lord Chancellor
must consult—

7.2.a

in relation to rules applicable to proceedings in England and Wales, the Lord
Chief Justice of England and Wales;

7.2.b

in relation to rules applicable to proceedings in Northern Ireland, the Lord
Chief Justice of Northern Ireland.

7.3

But the Lord Chancellor is not required to undertake any other consultation
before making the rules.

7.4

A requirement to consult under  sub-paragraph (2)  may be satisfied by
consultation that took place wholly or partly before this Schedule comes into
force.

7.5

Rules of court made by the Lord Chancellor under  sub-paragraph (1) —

7.5.a

must be laid before Parliament, and

7.5.b

if not approved by a resolution of each House before the end of 40 days
beginning with the day on which they were made, cease to have effect at the
end of that period.

7.6

In determining that period of 40 days no account is to be taken of any time
during which Parliament is dissolved or prorogued or during which both Houses
are adjourned for more than 4 days.

7.7

If rules cease to have effect in accordance with  sub-paragraph (5) —

7.7.a

that does not affect anything done in previous reliance on the rules, and

7.7.b

sub-paragraph (1)  applies again as if the rules had not been made.

7.8

The following provisions do not apply to rules of court made by the Lord
Chancellor under  this paragraph —

7.8.a

section 3(6) of the Civil Procedure Act 1997 (Parliamentary procedure for
civil procedure rules);

7.8.b

section 56(1), (2) and (4) of the Judicature (Northern Ireland) Act 1978
(statutory rules procedure).

7.9

Until the coming into force of section 85 of the Courts Act 2003, the
reference in sub-paragraph (8)(a) to section 3(6) of the Civil Procedure Act
1997 is to be read as a reference to section 3(2) of that Act.

##### Use of advisers

8

8.1

In any relevant proceedings or appeal proceedings the relevant court may if it
thinks fit—

8.1.a

call in aid one or more advisers appointed for the purposes of  this paragraph
by the Lord Chancellor, and

8.1.b

hear and dispose of the proceedings with the assistance of the adviser or
advisers.

8.2

The Lord Chancellor may appoint advisers for the purposes of  this paragraph
only with the approval of—

8.2.a

the Lord President of the Court of Session, in relation to an adviser who may
be called in aid wholly or mainly in Scotland;

8.2.b

the Lord Chief Justice of Northern Ireland, in relation to an adviser who may
be called in aid wholly or mainly in Northern Ireland;

8.2.c

the Lord Chief Justice of England and Wales, in any other case.

8.3

Rules of court may regulate the use of advisers in proceedings who are called
in aid under  sub-paragraph (1) .

8.4

The Lord Chancellor may pay such remuneration, expenses and allowances to
advisers appointed for the purposes of  this paragraph  as the Lord Chancellor
may determine.

9

9.1

The Lord President of the Court of Session may nominate a judge of the Court
of Session who is a member of the First or Second Division of the Inner House
of that Court to exercise the function under  paragraph 8 (2) (a) .

9.2

The Lord Chief Justice of Northern Ireland may nominate any of the following
to exercise the function under  paragraph 8 (2) (b) —

9.2.a

the holder of one of the offices listed in Schedule 1 to the Justice (Northern
Ireland) Act 2002;

9.2.b

a Lord Justice of Appeal (as defined in section 88 of that Act).

9.3

The Lord Chief Justice of England and Wales may nominate a judicial office
holder (as defined in section 109(4) of the Constitutional Reform Act 2005) to
exercise the function under  paragraph 8 (2) (c) .

##### Appointment of special advocate

10

10.1

The appropriate law officer may appoint a person to represent the interests of
a party in any relevant proceedings or appeal proceedings from which the party
(and any legal representative of the party) is excluded.

10.2

A person appointed under  sub-paragraph (1)  is referred to in  this Schedule
as appointed as a “special advocate”.

10.3

The “appropriate law officer” is—

10.3.a

in relation to proceedings in England and Wales, the Attorney General;

10.3.b

in relation to proceedings in Scotland, the Advocate General for Scotland;

10.3.c

in relation to proceedings in Northern Ireland, the Advocate General for
Northern Ireland.

10.4

A person appointed as a special advocate is not responsible to the party to
the proceedings whose interests the person is appointed to represent.

10.5

A person may be appointed as a special advocate only if—

10.5.a

in the case of an appointment by the Attorney General, the person has a
general qualification for the purposes of section 71 of the Courts and Legal
Services Act 1990;

10.5.b

in the case of an appointment by the Advocate General for Scotland, the person
is an advocate or a solicitor who has rights of audience in the Court of
Session or the High Court of Justiciary by virtue of section 25A of the
Solicitors (Scotland) Act 1980;

10.5.c

in the case of an appointment by the Advocate General for Northern Ireland,
the person is a member of the Bar of Northern Ireland.

Powers of entry, search, seizure and retention

Section 57

##### Introductory

1

This Schedule  confers powers of entry, search, seizure and retention on
constables in connection with the imposition of measures on individuals.

2

A power conferred on a constable by virtue of  this Schedule —

2.a

is additional to powers which the constable has at common law or by virtue of
any other enactment, and

2.b

is not to be taken as affecting those powers.

3

A constable may detain an individual for the purpose of carrying out a search
of that individual under a power conferred by virtue of  this Schedule .

4

A constable may use reasonable force, if necessary, for the purpose of
exercising a power conferred on the constable by virtue of  this Schedule .

##### Entry and search for purposes of serving a 

5

5.1

For the purpose of serving a relevant notice on an individual, a constable
may—

5.1.a

enter any premises where the constable has reasonable grounds for believing
the individual to be, and

5.1.b

search those premises for that individual.

5.2

A “ relevant notice ” means—

5.2.a

a  Part 2  notice;

5.2.b

a notice under  section 41 (2)  extending a  Part 2  notice;

5.2.c

a notice under  section 48 (1)  varying a  Part 2  notice as mentioned in
paragraph (c)  of that subsection; or

5.2.d

a notice under  section 49 (6)  reviving a  Part 2  notice.

##### Search of individual or premises at time of serving a 

6

6.1

This paragraph  applies if a  Part 2  notice is being, or has just been,
served on an individual.

6.2

A constable may (without a warrant)—

6.2.a

search the individual for the purpose mentioned in  sub-paragraph (3) ;

6.2.b

enter and search, for that purpose, any premises mentioned in  sub-paragraph
(4) .

6.3

The purpose is that of ascertaining whether there is anything on the
individual, or (as the case may be) in the premises, that contravenes measures
specified in the  Part 2  notice.

6.4

The premises referred to in  sub-paragraph (2) (b)  are—

6.4.a

the individual’s place of residence;

6.4.b

other premises to which the individual has power to grant access.

6.5

A constable may seize anything that the constable finds in the course of a
search carried out under a power conferred by  this paragraph —

6.5.a

for the purpose of ascertaining whether measures specified in the  Part 2
notice are being or are about to be contravened by the individual;

6.5.b

for the purpose of securing compliance by the individual with measures
specified in the  Part 2  notice;

6.5.c

if the constable has reasonable grounds for suspecting that—

6.5.c.i

the thing is or contains evidence in relation to an offence, and

6.5.c.ii

it is necessary to seize it in order to prevent it being concealed, lost,
damaged, altered or destroyed.

##### Search of premises on suspicion of absconding

7

7.1

This paragraph  applies if a constable reasonably suspects that an individual
in respect of whom a  Part 2  notice is in force has absconded.

7.2

The constable may (without a warrant) enter and search any premises mentioned
in  sub-paragraph (3) —

7.2.a

for the purposes of determining whether the individual has absconded;

7.2.b

if it appears that the individual has absconded, for anything that may assist
in the pursuit and arrest of the individual.

7.3

The premises referred to in  sub-paragraph (2)  are—

7.3.a

the individual's place of residence;

7.3.b

other premises to which the individual has power to grant access;

7.3.c

any premises to which the individual had power to grant access and with which
there is reason to believe that the individual is or was recently connected.

7.4

A constable may seize anything that the constable finds in the course of a
search carried out under a power conferred by  this paragraph —

7.4.a

if the constable reasonably believes that the thing will assist in the pursuit
or arrest of the individual;

7.4.b

if the constable has reasonable grounds for suspecting that—

7.4.b.i

the thing is or contains evidence in relation to an offence, and

7.4.b.ii

it is necessary to seize it in order to prevent it being concealed, lost,
damaged, altered or destroyed.

##### Search for compliance purposes

8

8.1

A constable may apply for the issue of a warrant under  this paragraph  for
the purpose of determining whether an individual in respect of whom a  Part 2
notice is in force is complying with measures specified in the notice.

8.2

A warrant under  this paragraph  may authorise a constable to do either or
both of the following—

8.2.a

to search the individual;

8.2.b

to enter and search the individual’s place of residence or any other premises
that are specified in the warrant.

8.3

An application for a warrant under  this paragraph  must be made to the
appropriate judicial authority.

8.4

The appropriate judicial authority may, on such an application, grant the
warrant only if satisfied that the warrant is necessary for the purpose
mentioned in  sub-paragraph (1) .

8.5

A constable may seize anything that the constable finds in the course of a
search carried out under a power conferred by a warrant issued under  this
paragraph —

8.5.a

for the purpose of ascertaining whether any measure specified in the  Part 2
notice has been, is being, or is about to be, contravened by the individual;

8.5.b

for the purpose of securing compliance by the individual with measures
specified in the  Part 2  notice;

8.5.c

if the constable has reasonable grounds for suspecting that—

8.5.c.i

the thing is or contains evidence in relation to an offence, and

8.5.c.ii

it is necessary to seize it in order to prevent it being concealed, lost,
damaged, altered or destroyed.

8.6

In  this paragraph  “ appropriate judicial authority ”, in relation to a
warrant, means—

8.6.a

a justice of the peace, if the application for the warrant is made in England
or Wales;

8.6.b

a sheriff, if the application is made in Scotland;

8.6.c

a lay magistrate, if the application is made in Northern Ireland.

9

9.1

This paragraph  applies in relation to a warrant issued in England, Wales or
Northern Ireland under  paragraph 8  so far as it authorises a constable to
search an individual.

9.2

In relation to warrants issued under that paragraph so far as authorising the
entry and search of premises, see—

9.2.a

sections 15 and 16 of the Police and Criminal Evidence Act 1984, in relation
to warrants issued in England and Wales;

9.2.b

Articles 17 and 18 of the Police and Criminal Evidence (Northern Ireland)
Order 1989 ( S.I. 1989/1341 (N.I. 12) ), in relation to warrants issued in
Northern Ireland.

9.3

The constable applying for the warrant must—

9.3.a

state the ground on which the application is made, and

9.3.b

identify, so far as practicable, the articles to be sought.

9.4

The application for the warrant is to be made without notice and—

9.4.a

if made in England or Wales, supported by an information in writing;

9.4.b

if made in Northern Ireland, supported by a complaint in writing and
substantiated on oath.

9.5

The constable must answer on oath any questions that the appropriate judicial
authority (within the meaning of  paragraph 8 ) hearing the application may
ask of the constable.

9.6

If the warrant is issued it authorises a search of the individual on one
occasion only.

9.7

The warrant must—

9.7.a

specify the name of the constable applying for it, the date on which it is
issued and the fact that it is issued under  paragraph 8 , and

9.7.b

identify, so far as practicable, the articles to be sought.

9.8

Two copies must be made of the warrant and clearly certified as copies.

9.9

The warrant may be executed by any constable.

9.10

The search under the warrant must be carried out within 28 days of its issue.

9.11

The search must be carried out at a reasonable hour unless it appears to the
constable executing the warrant that the purposes of the search may be
frustrated if carried out then.

9.12

The constable seeking to execute the warrant must, before carrying out the
search—

9.12.a

identify himself or herself to the individual,

9.12.b

if not in uniform, produce documentary evidence that he or she is a constable
to the individual,

9.12.c

produce the warrant to the individual, and

9.12.d

supply the individual with a copy of the warrant (which, in Northern Ireland,
must be a certified copy).

9.13

The constable executing the warrant must make an endorsement on it stating—

9.13.a

whether anything sought was found in the course of the search, and

9.13.b

whether anything was seized.

9.14

When the warrant has been executed it must be returned to the designated
officer.

9.15

The designated officer must retain a warrant returned under  sub-paragraph
(14)  for a period of 12 months from the time of its return and, if requested
during that period, allow the individual to inspect it.

9.16

The “designated officer” is—

9.16.a

in relation to a warrant issued in England and Wales, the designated officer
for the local justice area in which the justice of the peace who issued the
warrant was acting when it was issued;

9.16.b

in relation to a warrant issued in Northern Ireland, the clerk of petty
sessions.

##### Search of individual for public safety purposes

10

10.1

A constable may (without a warrant) search an individual in respect of whom a
Part 2  notice is in force for the purpose of ascertaining whether the
individual is in possession of anything that could be used to threaten or harm
any person.

10.2

The power of a constable to search the individual under  this paragraph  may
be exercised—

10.2.a

following entry onto premises by virtue of this Part, or

10.2.b

at any other time when the constable is in the presence of the individual.

10.3

A constable may seize anything that the constable finds in the course of a
search carried out under a power conferred by  this paragraph —

10.3.a

if the constable has reasonable grounds for suspecting that the thing may be
used to threaten or harm any person;

10.3.b

if the constable has reasonable grounds for suspecting that—

10.3.b.i

the thing is or contains evidence in relation to an offence, and

10.3.b.ii

it is necessary to seize it to prevent it being concealed, lost, damaged,
altered or destroyed.

##### Power to retain items

11

11.1

Anything that is seized under a power conferred by virtue of  this Schedule
may be—

11.1.a

subjected to tests;

11.1.b

retained for as long as is necessary in all the circumstances.

11.2

In particular (and regardless of the ground on which the thing was seized)—

11.2.a

if a constable has reasonable grounds for believing that the thing is or
contains evidence in relation to an offence, it may be retained—

11.2.a.i

for use as evidence at a trial for an offence, or

11.2.a.ii

for forensic examination or for investigation in connection with an offence,
and

11.2.b

if a constable has reasonable grounds for believing that the thing has been
obtained in consequence of the commission of an offence, it may be retained in
order to establish its lawful owner.

11.3

Nothing may be retained for either of the purposes mentioned in  sub-paragraph
(2) (a)  if a photograph or copy would be sufficient for that purpose.

11.4

Nothing in  this paragraph  or in  paragraph 12  affects any power of a court
to make an order under section 1 of the Police (Property) Act 1897.

12

12.1

This paragraph  applies if—

12.1.a

a device is surrendered by virtue of a condition of the kind mentioned in
paragraph 8 (4) (e)  of  Schedule 7  (surrendering of electronic communication
devices for inspection or modification purposes), and

12.1.b

a constable has reasonable grounds for believing that the device is or
contains evidence in relation to an offence.

12.2

The device may be seized and retained for as long as is necessary in all the
circumstances.

12.3

In particular—

12.3.a

the thing may be retained—

12.3.a.i

for use as evidence at a trial for an offence, or

12.3.a.ii

for forensic examination or for investigation in connection with an offence,
and

12.3.b

if a constable has reasonable grounds for believing that the device has been
obtained in consequence of the commission of an offence, it may be retained in
order to establish its lawful owner.

12.4

Nothing may be retained for either of the purposes mentioned in  sub-paragraph
(3) (a)  if a photograph or copy would be sufficient for that purpose.

Fingerprints and samples

Section 58

##### Taking of fingerprints and samples: England, Wales and Northern Ireland

1

1.1

This paragraph  applies at any time when a  Part 2  notice is in force in
respect of an individual in England, Wales or Northern Ireland.

1.2

A constable may take fingerprints or a non-intimate sample from the
individual—

1.2.a

with the consent of the individual given in writing, or

1.2.b

without that consent.

1.3

A constable may use reasonable force, if necessary, for the purpose of
exercising the power under  sub-paragraph (2) (b) .

1.4

Before any fingerprints or a non-intimate sample are taken the individual must
be informed—

1.4.a

of the reason for taking the fingerprints or sample,

1.4.b

of the fact that the fingerprints or sample are taken under the power
conferred by  this paragraph , and

1.4.c

that the fingerprints or sample may be the subject of a relevant search.

1.5

The matters mentioned in  sub-paragraph (4)  must be recorded as soon as
practicable after the fingerprints or non-intimate sample are taken.

1.6

The information mentioned in  sub-paragraph (4)  must be given by—

1.6.a

the constable taking the fingerprints or non-intimate sample, or

1.6.b

if the fingerprints or non-intimate sample are taken at a police station (see
paragraph 3 ), any other officer.

1.7

Where a sample of hair other than pubic hair is to be taken under  this
paragraph , the sample may be taken either by cutting hairs or by plucking
hairs with their roots so long as no more are plucked than the person taking
the sample reasonably considers to be necessary for a sufficient sample.

2

2.1

A constable may exercise the power under  paragraph 1  to take fingerprints or
a non-intimate sample from an individual only if at the time when the power is
to be exercised—

2.1.a

in the case of fingerprints, the condition in  sub-paragraph (2)  is met;

2.1.b

in the case of a sample, the condition in  sub-paragraph (3)  is met.

2.2

The condition in the case of fingerprints is that—

2.2.a

the individual has not had fingerprints taken under  paragraph 1  on a
previous occasion after the time at which the present  Part 2  notice came
into force, or

2.2.b

fingerprints were so taken on a previous occasion after that time but—

2.2.b.i

the fingerprints taken do not constitute a complete set of the individual's
fingerprints, or

2.2.b.ii

some or all of the fingerprints taken are not of sufficient quality to allow
satisfactory analysis, comparison or matching.

2.3

The condition in the case of a non-intimate sample is that—

2.3.a

the individual has not had a sample of the same type and from the same part of
the body taken under  paragraph 1  on a previous occasion after the time at
which the present  Part 2  notice came into force, or

2.3.b

a sample was so taken on a previous occasion after that time but it proved
insufficient.

2.4

In  this paragraph  “the present  Part 2  notice” means the  Part 2  notice in
force at the time when it is proposed to exercise the power to take the
fingerprints or sample.

3

3.1

A constable may—

3.1.a

require an individual to attend a police station for the purposes of taking
fingerprints or a non-intimate sample from the individual under  paragraph 1 ,
and

3.1.b

arrest without warrant an individual who fails to comply with such a
requirement.

3.2

A requirement under  sub-paragraph (1) (a) —

3.2.a

must give the individual a period of at least 7 days within which the
individual must attend the police station (subject to  sub-paragraph (4) ),
and

3.2.b

may direct the individual to attend at a specified time of day or between
specified times of day.

3.3

In specifying a period or time or times of day for the purposes of  sub-
paragraph (2) , the constable must consider whether the fingerprints or non-
intimate sample could reasonably be taken at a time when the individual is for
any other reason required to attend the police station (including, in
particular, under measures imposed on the individual by virtue of  paragraph
11  of  Schedule 7 ).

3.4

In giving a requirement under  this paragraph  a constable may specify a
period of shorter than 7 days if—

3.4.a

there is an urgent need for the fingerprints or sample for the purposes of the
investigation of an offence, and

3.4.b

the shorter period is authorised by an officer of at least the rank of
inspector.

3.5

Where an authorisation is given under  sub-paragraph (4) (b) —

3.5.a

the fact of the authorisation, and

3.5.b

the reasons for giving it,

must be recorded as soon as practicable after it has been given.

3.6

If the constable who gives a requirement to an individual under  this
paragraph  and the individual agree, it may be varied so as to specify any
period within which, or date or time at which, the individual must attend; but
a variation does not have effect unless confirmed by the constable in writing.

##### Taking of relevant physical data and samples: Scotland

4

4.1

This paragraph  applies at any time when a  Part 2  notice is in force in
respect of an individual in Scotland.

4.2

A constable may—

4.2.a

take from the individual, or require the individual to provide, any relevant
physical data;

4.2.b

with the authority of an officer of a rank no lower than inspector, take from
the individual any sample mentioned in paragraph (a), (b) or (c) of subsection
(6) of section 18 of the Criminal Procedure (Scotland) Act 1995 (prints,
samples etc in criminal investigations) by the means specified in that
paragraph in relation to the sample;

4.2.c

take, or direct a police custody and security officer to take, from the
individual a sample mentioned in subsection (6A) of that section by the means
specified in that subsection.

4.3

A constable may—

4.3.a

require the individual to attend a police station for the purposes mentioned
in  sub-paragraph (2) , and

4.3.b

arrest without warrant an individual who fails to comply with such a
requirement.

4.4

A requirement under  sub-paragraph (3) (a) —

4.4.a

must give the individual at least 7 days’ notice of the date on which the
individual is required to attend the police station, and

4.4.b

may direct the individual to attend at a specified time of day or between
specified times of day.

4.5

In specifying a date or time or times of day for the purposes of  sub-
paragraph (4) , the constable must consider whether the relevant physical data
or sample could reasonably be taken at a time when the individual is for any
other reason required to attend the police station (including, in particular,
under measures imposed on the individual by virtue of  paragraph 11  of
Schedule 7 ).

4.6

A constable may use reasonable force, if necessary, in—

4.6.a

taking any relevant physical data under  sub-paragraph (2) (a) ,

4.6.b

securing compliance with a requirement imposed by the constable under that
sub-paragraph, or

4.6.c

taking any sample under  sub-paragraph (2) (b) .

4.7

A constable may, with the authority of an officer of a rank no lower than
inspector, use reasonable force, if necessary, in taking any sample under
sub-paragraph (2) (c) .

4.8

In  this paragraph  “ police custody and security officer ” has the same
meaning as in Part 1 of the  Police and Fire Reform (Scotland) Act 2012 (asp
8)  (see section 99 of that Act).

##### Checking of fingerprints, samples etc

5

Any fingerprints, data or samples obtained under  paragraph 1  or  4 , or
information derived from such samples, may be checked against—

5.a

other such fingerprints, data or samples or any information derived from such
samples;

5.b

any fingerprints or samples taken under paragraph  10  or  12  of  Schedule 6
or any information derived from such samples;

5.c

any fingerprints, samples or information mentioned in section 63A(1)(a) or (b)
of the Police and Criminal Evidence Act 1984;

5.d

any fingerprints, samples or information mentioned in Article 63A(1)(a) and
(b) of the Police and Criminal Evidence (Northern Ireland) Order 1989 ( S.I.
1989/1341 (N.I. 12) );

5.e

any fingerprints or samples taken under  paragraph 10  or  12  of Schedule 8
to the Terrorism Act 2000 or any information derived from such samples;

5.f

any of the relevant physical data, samples or information mentioned in section
19C(1) of the Criminal Procedure (Scotland) Act 1995;

5.g

any of the relevant physical data, samples or information held by virtue of
section 56 of the  Criminal Justice (Scotland) Act 2003 (asp 7) ;

5.h

material to which section 18 of the Counter-Terrorism Act 2008 applies;

5.i

any of the fingerprints, data or samples obtained under paragraph 1 or 4 of
Schedule 6 to the Terrorism Prevention and Investigation Measures Act 2011, or
information derived from such samples;

5.j

any fingerprints or samples taken under paragraph 34 of Schedule 3 to the
Counter-Terrorism and Border Security Act 2019 or any information derived from
such samples.

##### Requirement to destroy material

6

6.1

This paragraph  applies to—

6.1.a

fingerprints taken under  paragraph 1 ,

6.1.b

a DNA profile derived from a DNA sample taken under that paragraph,

6.1.c

relevant physical data taken or provided under  paragraph 4 ,

6.1.d

a DNA profile derived from a DNA sample taken under that paragraph.

6.2

Fingerprints, relevant physical data and DNA profiles to which  this paragraph
applies (“ paragraph 6  material”) must be destroyed if it appears to the
responsible chief officer of police that the taking or providing of the
material or, in the case of a DNA profile, the taking of the sample from which
the DNA profile was derived, was unlawful.

6.3

In any other case,  paragraph 6  material must be destroyed unless it is
retained under a power conferred by  paragraph 8 , 9, or  11 .

6.4

Paragraph 6  material that ceases to be retained under a power mentioned in
sub-paragraph (3)  may continue to be retained under any other such power that
applies to it.

6.5

Nothing in  this paragraph  prevents a relevant search from being carried out,
in relation to  paragraph 6  material, within such time as may reasonably be
required for the search if the responsible chief officer of police considers
the search to be desirable.

7

7.1

If fingerprints or relevant physical data are required by  paragraph 6  to be
destroyed, any copies of the fingerprints or data held by a police force must
also be destroyed.

7.2

If a DNA profile is required by that paragraph to be destroyed, no copy may be
retained by a police force except in a form which does not include information
which identifies the individual to whom the DNA profile relates.

##### Retention of 

8

8.1

This paragraph  applies to  paragraph 6  material taken from, or provided by,
an individual who has no previous convictions or (in the case of England and
Wales or Northern Ireland) only one exempt conviction.

8.2

The  material may be retained until the end of the period of 6 months
beginning with the date on which the  Part 2  notice that was in force when
the material was taken ceases to be in force (subject to  sub-paragraphs (3)
and  (4) ).

8.3

If, before the end of that period, the  Part 2  notice is quashed by the court
under this Part, the material may be retained only until there is no
possibility of an appeal against—

8.3.a

the decision to quash the notice, or

8.3.b

any decision made on an appeal against that decision.

8.4

If, after a  Part 2  notice is quashed or otherwise ceases to be in force,
measures are imposed on the individual (whether by the revival of a  Part 2
notice or the imposition of a new  Part 2  notice)—

8.4.a

within the period for which material in relation to the individual is retained
by virtue of  sub-paragraph (2) , or

8.4.b

within, or immediately after the end of, the period for which such material is
retained by virtue of  sub-paragraph (3) ,

sub-paragraphs (2)  and  (3)  apply again for the purposes of the retention of
that material (taking references to the  Part 2  notice as references to the
revived or new  Part 2  notice).

8.5

In determining whether there is no further possibility of an appeal against a
decision of the kind mentioned in  sub-paragraph (3) , any power to extend the
time for giving notice of application for leave to appeal, or for applying for
leave to appeal, must be ignored.

9

9.1

This paragraph  applies to paragraph  6  material taken from, or provided by,
an individual—

9.1.a

who has been convicted of a recordable offence (other than a single exempt
conviction) or of an offence in Scotland which is punishable by imprisonment,
or

9.1.b

who is so convicted before the end of the period within which the material may
be retained by virtue of  paragraph 8 .

9.2

The material may be retained indefinitely.

10

10.1

For the purposes of paragraphs  8  and  9  an individual is to be treated as
having been convicted of an offence if—

10.1.a

in relation to a recordable offence in England and Wales or Northern Ireland—

10.1.a.i

the individual has been given a caution or youth caution in respect of the
offence which, at the time of the caution, the individual has admitted,

10.1.a.ii

the individual has been found not guilty of the offence by reason of insanity,
or

10.1.a.iii

the individual has been found to be under a disability and to have done the
act charged in respect of the offence,

10.1.b

the individual, in relation to an offence in Scotland punishable by
imprisonment, has accepted or has been deemed to accept—

10.1.b.i

a conditional offer under section 302 of the Criminal Procedure (Scotland) Act
1995,

10.1.b.ii

a compensation offer under section 302A of that Act,

10.1.b.iii

a combined offer under section 302B of that Act, or

10.1.b.iv

a work offer under section 303ZA of that Act,

10.1.c

the individual, in relation to an offence in Scotland punishable by
imprisonment, has been acquitted on account of the individual’s insanity at
the time of the offence or (as the case may be) by virtue of section 51A of
the Criminal Procedure (Scotland) Act 1995,

10.1.d

a finding in respect of the individual has been made under section 55(2) of
the Criminal Procedure (Scotland) Act 1995 in relation to an offence in
Scotland punishable by imprisonment,

10.1.e

the individual, having been given a fixed penalty notice under section 129(1)
of the  Antisocial Behaviour etc. (Scotland) Act 2004 (asp 8)  in connection
with an offence in Scotland punishable by imprisonment, has paid—

10.1.e.i

the fixed penalty, or

10.1.e.ii

(as the case may be) the sum which the individual is liable to pay by virtue
of section 131(5) of that Act, or

10.1.f

the individual, in relation to an offence in Scotland punishable by
imprisonment, has been discharged absolutely by order under section 246(3) of
the Criminal Procedure (Scotland) Act 1995.

10.2

Paragraphs  8 ,  9  and  this paragraph , so far as they relate to individuals
convicted of an offence, have effect despite anything in the Rehabilitation of
Offenders Act 1974 or the Rehabilitation of Offenders (Northern Ireland) Order
1978 ( S.I. 1978/1908 (N.I. 27) ).

10.3

But a person is not to be treated as having been convicted of an offence if
that conviction is a disregarded conviction or caution by virtue of section 92
or 101A of the Protection of Freedoms Act 2012.

10.4

For the purposes of paragraphs  8  and  9 —

10.4.a

an individual has no previous convictions if the individual has not previously
been convicted—

10.4.a.i

in England and Wales or Northern Ireland of a recordable offence, or

10.4.a.ii

in Scotland of an offence which is punishable by imprisonment, and

10.4.b

if the individual has previously been convicted of a recordable offence in
England and Wales or Northern Ireland, the conviction is exempt if it is in
respect of a recordable offence, other than a qualifying offence, committed
when the individual was aged under 18.

10.5

In sub-paragraph  (4)  “qualifying offence”—

10.5.a

in relation to a conviction in respect of a recordable offence committed in
England and Wales, has the meaning given by section 65A of the Police and
Criminal Evidence Act 1984, and

10.5.b

in relation to a conviction in respect of a recordable offence committed in
Northern Ireland, has the meaning given by Article 53A of the Police and
Criminal Evidence (Northern Ireland) Order 1989 ( S.I. 1989/1341 (N.I. 12) ).

10.6

For the purposes of  sub-paragraph (4) —

10.6.a

a person is to be treated as having previously been convicted in England and
Wales of a recordable offence if—

10.6.a.i

the person has previously been convicted of an offence under the law of a
country or territory outside the United Kingdom, and

10.6.a.ii

the act constituting the offence would constitute a recordable offence under
the law of England and Wales if done there (whether or not it constituted such
an offence when the person was convicted);

10.6.b

a person is to be treated as having previously been convicted in Northern
Ireland of a recordable offence if—

10.6.b.i

the person has previously been convicted of an offence under the law of a
country or territory outside the United Kingdom, and

10.6.b.ii

the act constituting the offence would constitute a recordable offence under
the law of Northern Ireland if done there (whether or not it constituted such
an offence when the person was convicted);

10.6.c

a person is to be treated as having previously been convicted in Scotland of
an offence which is punishable by imprisonment if—

10.6.c.i

the person has previously been convicted of an offence under the law of a
country or territory outside the United Kingdom, and

10.6.c.ii

the act constituting the offence would constitute an offence punishable by
imprisonment under the law of Scotland if done there (whether or not it
constituted such an offence when the person was convicted);

10.6.d

the reference in  sub-paragraph (4) (b)  to a qualifying offence includes a
reference to an offence under the law of a country or territory outside the
United Kingdom where the act constituting the offence would constitute a
qualifying offence under the law of England and Wales if done there or (as the
case may be) under the law of Northern Ireland if done there (whether or not
it constituted such an offence when the person was convicted).

10.7

For the purposes of paragraph  8 ,  9  or  this paragraph —

10.7.a

“ offence ”, in relation to any country or territory outside the United
Kingdom, includes an act punishable under the law of that country or
territory, however it is described;

10.7.b

a person has in particular been convicted of an offence under the law of a
country or territory outside the United Kingdom if—

10.7.b.i

a court exercising jurisdiction under the law of that country or territory has
made in respect of such an offence a finding equivalent to a finding that the
person is not guilty by reason of insanity, or

10.7.b.ii

such a court has made in respect of such an offence a finding equivalent to a
finding that the person is under a disability and did the act charged against
the person in respect of the offence.

10.8

If an individual is convicted of more than one offence arising out of a single
course of action, those convictions are to be treated as a single conviction
for the purposes of calculating under paragraph  8  or  9  whether the
individual has been convicted of one offence.

11

11.1

Paragraph 6  material may be retained for as long as a national security
determination made by a chief officer of police has effect in relation to it.

11.2

A national security determination is made if a chief officer of police
determines that it is necessary for any  paragraph 6  material to be retained
for the purposes of national security.

11.3

A national security determination—

11.3.a

must be in writing,

11.3.b

has effect for a maximum of 5 years beginning with the date on which the
determination is made, and

11.3.c

may be renewed.

11.4

In  this paragraph  “ chief officer of police ” means—

11.4.a

a chief officer of police of a police force in England and Wales,

11.4.b

the chief constable of the Police Service of Scotland,

11.4.c

the Chief Constable of the Police Service of Northern Ireland,

11.4.d

the Chief Constable of the Ministry of Defence Police,

11.4.e

the Chief Constable of the British Transport Police Force, or

11.4.f

the Director General of the National Crime Agency.

12

12.1

This paragraph  applies where  paragraph 6  material is or includes a person’s
fingerprints (“the original fingerprints”).

12.2

A constable may make a determination under  this paragraph  in respect of any
further fingerprints taken from, or provided by, the same person (“the further
fingerprints”) if conditions 1 and 2 are met.

12.3

Condition 1 is met if the further fingerprints—

12.3.a

are  paragraph 6  material,

12.3.b

are taken or provided under or by virtue of—

12.3.b.i

Part 5 of the Police and Criminal Evidence Act 1984,

12.3.b.ii

Article 61 of the Police and Criminal Evidence (Northern Ireland) Order 1989 (
S.I. 1989/1341 (N.I. 12) ),

12.3.b.iii

any provision, power or authority mentioned in section 18G(1) of the Criminal
Procedure (Scotland) Act 1995,

12.3.b.iv

paragraph 10 of Schedule 8 to the Terrorism Act 2000,

12.3.b.v

paragraph 34 of Schedule 3 to the Counter-Terrorism and Border Security Act
2019, or

12.3.b.vi

paragraph  10  of  Schedule 6 , or

12.3.c

are material to which section 18 of the Counter-Terrorism Act 2008 applies.

12.4

Condition 2 is met if—

12.4.a

in a case where the further fingerprints are material to which section 18 of
the Counter-Terrorism Act 2008 applies, the original fingerprints and the
further fingerprints are held under the law of the same part of the United
Kingdom;

12.4.b

in any other case, the original fingerprints and the further fingerprints were
taken from or provided by the person in the same part of the United Kingdom.

12.5

Where a determination under  this paragraph  is made in respect of the further
fingerprints—

12.5.a

the further fingerprints may be retained for as long as the original
fingerprints are retained under any power conferred by  paragraph 8 , 9 or  11
, and

12.5.b

a requirement under any enactment to destroy the further fingerprints does not
apply for as long as their retention is authorised by  paragraph (a) .

12.6

Sub-paragraph (5) (a)  does not prevent the further fingerprints being
retained after the original fingerprints fall to be destroyed if the continued
retention of the further fingerprints is authorised under any enactment.

12.7

A written record must be made of a determination under  this paragraph .

12.8

In  this paragraph  references to a part of the United Kingdom are references
to—

12.8.a

England and Wales,

12.8.b

Scotland, or

12.8.c

Northern Ireland.

##### Requirement to destroy samples

13

13.1

This paragraph  applies to—

13.1.a

non-intimate samples taken under  paragraph 1 , or

13.1.b

samples taken under  paragraph 4 (2) (b)  or  (c) .

13.2

Samples to which  this paragraph  applies must be destroyed if it appears to
the responsible chief officer of police that the taking of the sample was
unlawful.

13.3

Subject to this, the rule in  sub-paragraph (4)  or (as the case may be)  (5)
applies.

13.4

A DNA sample to which  this paragraph  applies must be destroyed—

13.4.a

as soon as a DNA profile has been derived from the sample, or

13.4.b

if sooner, before the end of the period of 6 months beginning with the date on
which the sample was taken.

13.5

Any other sample to which  this paragraph  applies must be destroyed before
the end of the period of 6 months beginning with the date on which it was
taken.

13.6

Nothing in  this paragraph  prevents a relevant search, in relation to samples
to which  this paragraph  applies, from being carried out within such time as
may reasonably be required for the search if the responsible chief officer of
police considers the search to be desirable.

##### Use of retained material

14

14.1

Any material to which  paragraph 6  or  13  applies must not be used other
than—

14.1.a

in the interests of national security,

14.1.b

for the purposes of investigating foreign power threat activity,

14.1.c

for the purposes of a terrorist investigation (within the meaning of the
Terrorism Act 2000),

14.1.d

for purposes related to the prevention or detection of crime, the
investigation of an offence or the conduct of a prosecution, or

14.1.e

for purposes related to the identification of a deceased person or of the
person to whom the material relates.

14.2

Material which is required by  paragraph 6  or  13  to be destroyed must not
at any time after it is required to be destroyed be used—

14.2.a

in evidence against the individual to whom the material relates, or

14.2.b

for the purposes of the investigation of any offence.

14.3

In  this paragraph —

14.3.a

the reference to using material includes a reference to allowing any check to
be made against it and to disclosing it to any person,

14.3.b

the reference to crime includes a reference to any conduct which—

14.3.b.i

constitutes one or more criminal offences (whether under the law of a part of
the United Kingdom or of a country or territory outside the United Kingdom),
or

14.3.b.ii

is, or corresponds to, any conduct which, if it all took place in any one part
of the United Kingdom, would constitute one or more criminal offences, and

14.3.c

the references to an investigation and to a prosecution include references,
respectively, to any investigation outside the United Kingdom of any crime or
suspected crime and to a prosecution brought in respect of any crime in a
country or territory outside the United Kingdom.

##### Interpretation

15

15.1

In  this Schedule —

“ DNA profile ” means any information derived from a DNA sample; “ DNA sample
” means any material that has come from a human body and consists of or
includes human cells; “ fingerprints ” has the meaning given by section 65(1)
of the Police and Criminal Evidence Act 1984 or, in Northern Ireland, Article
53(1) of the Police and Criminal Evidence (Northern Ireland) Order 1989 ( S.I.
1989/1341 (N.I.12) ); “ non-intimate sample ” has the meaning given by section
65(1) of the Police and Criminal Evidence Act 1984 or, in Northern Ireland,
Article 53(1) of the Police and Criminal Evidence (Northern Ireland) Order
1989 ( S.I. 1989/1341 (N.I.12) ); “ paragraph 6 material ” has the meaning
given by  paragraph 6 (2) ; “ police force ” means any of the following— the
metropolitan police force; a police force maintained under  section 2  of the
Police Act 1996 (police forces in England and Wales outside London); the City
of London police force; the Police Service of Scotland; the Police Service of
Northern Ireland; the Police Service of Northern Ireland Reserve; the Ministry
of Defence Police; the National Crime Agency; the British Transport Police
Force; “ recordable offence ” has— in relation to a conviction in England and
Wales, the meaning given by section 118(1) of the Police and Criminal Evidence
Act 1984, and in relation to a conviction in Northern Ireland, the meaning
given by Article 2(2) of the Police and Criminal Evidence (Northern Ireland)
Order 1989 ( S.I. 1989/1341 (N.I. 12) ); “ relevant physical data ” has the
meaning given by section 18(7A) of the Criminal Procedure (Scotland) Act 1995;
“ relevant search ” means a search carried out for the purpose of checking any
fingerprints, samples, data or information against any of the fingerprints,
samples, data or information mentioned in  paragraph 5 (a)  to (k) ; “
responsible chief officer of police ” means— in relation to fingerprints or
samples taken by a constable of the Ministry of Defence Police, or a DNA
profile derived from a sample so taken, the Chief Constable of the Ministry of
Defence Police; in relation to fingerprints or samples taken by a constable of
the British Transport Police Force, or a DNA profile derived from a sample so
taken, the Chief Constable of the British Transport Police Force; in relation
to fingerprints or samples taken by a constable who is a National Crime Agency
officer, or a DNA profile derived from a sample so taken, the Director General
of the National Crime Agency; otherwise— in relation to fingerprints or
samples taken in England or Wales, or a DNA profile derived from a sample so
taken, the chief officer of police for the relevant police area; in relation
to relevant physical data or samples taken or provided in Scotland, or a DNA
profile derived from a sample so taken, the chief constable of the Police
Service of Scotland; in relation to fingerprints or samples taken in Northern
Ireland, or a DNA profile derived from a sample so taken, the Chief Constable
of the Police Service of Northern Ireland; “ sufficient ” and “ insufficient
”, in relation to a sample, have the same meaning as in Part 5 of the Police
and Criminal Evidence Act 1984 (see section 65(1) and (2) of that Act) or, in
Northern Ireland, Part 6 of the Police and Criminal Evidence (Northern
Ireland) Order 1989 ( S.I. 1989/1341 (N.I.12) ) (see Article 53(1) and (3) of
that Order).

15.2

In the definition of “responsible chief officer of police” in  sub-paragraph
(1) , in paragraph (d)(i), “ relevant police area ” means the police area—

15.2.a

in which the material concerned was taken, or

15.2.b

in the case of a DNA profile, in which the sample from which the DNA profile
was derived was taken.

                 Control of a person by a foreign power

Section 66

##### Conditions for control

1

1.1

A person is controlled by a foreign power if one or more of the following
conditions are met.

1.2

Condition 1 is that the foreign power has the right to direct or control, or
actually directs or controls, the person’s activities (in whole or in part).

1.3

Condition 2 is that the foreign power holds, directly or indirectly, more than
25% of the shares in the person.

1.4

Condition 3 is that the foreign power holds, directly or indirectly, more than
25% of the voting rights in the person.

1.5

Condition 4 is that the foreign power holds the right, directly or indirectly,
to appoint or remove an officer of the person.

1.6

Condition 5 is that—

1.6.a

the trustees of a trust, or the members of a partnership, unincorporated
association or other entity, that is not a legal person under the law by which
it is governed meet one or more of conditions 1 to 4 (in their capacity as
such) in relation to the person, and

1.6.b

the foreign power has the right to direct or control, or actually directs or
controls, the activities of that trust or entity (in whole or in part).

2

In this Schedule “officer”—

2.a

in relation to a body corporate, means a director, member of the committee of
management, chief executive, manager, secretary or other similar officer of
the body, or a person purporting to act in any such capacity;

2.b

in relation to a partnership, means a partner or person purporting to act as a
partner;

2.c

in relation to an unincorporated association other than a partnership, means a
person who is concerned in the management or control of the association or
purports to act in the capacity of a person so concerned.

##### Interpretation of 

###### Interpretation

3

This Part makes provision about the interpretation of Part 1 of this Schedule.

###### Joint interests

4

If a foreign power holds a share or right jointly with another person (whether
or not a foreign power), each of those persons is to be taken to hold that
share or right.

###### Joint arrangements

5

5.1

If shares or rights held by a foreign power and shares or rights held by
another person (whether or not a foreign power) are the subject of a joint
arrangement between those persons, each of those persons is to be taken to
hold the combined shares or rights of both persons.

5.2

A “joint arrangement” is an arrangement between the holders of shares (or
rights) that they will exercise all or substantially all the rights conferred
by their respective shares (or rights) jointly in a way that is pre-determined
by the arrangement.

5.3

For the meaning of “arrangement”, see  paragraph 12 .

###### Calculating shareholdings

6

6.1

In relation to a person that has a share capital, a reference to holding more
than 25% of the shares in that person is to holding shares comprised in the
issued share capital of that person of a nominal value exceeding (in
aggregate) 25% of that share capital.

6.2

In relation to a person that does not have a share capital—

6.2.a

a reference to holding shares in that person is to holding a right to share in
the capital or, as the case may be, profits of that person;

6.2.b

a reference to holding more than 25% of the shares in that person is to
holding a right or rights to share in more than 25% of the capital or, as the
case may be, profits of that person.

###### Voting rights

7

7.1

A reference to the voting rights in a person is to the rights conferred on
shareholders in respect of their shares (or, in the case of a person not
having a share capital, on members) to vote at general meetings of the person
on all or substantially all matters.

7.2

In relation to a person that does not have general meetings at which matters
are decided by the exercise of voting rights—

7.2.a

a reference to exercising voting rights in the person is to be read as a
reference to exercising rights in relation to the person that are equivalent
to those of a person entitled to exercise voting rights in a company;

7.2.b

a reference to exercising more than 25% of the voting rights in the person is
to be read as a reference to exercising the rights under the constitution of
the person to block changes to the overall policy of the person or to the
terms of its constitution.

8

In applying this Schedule, the voting rights in a person are to be reduced by
any rights held by that person.

###### Shares or rights held “indirectly”

9

9.1

A foreign power holds a share “indirectly” if the foreign power has a majority
stake in a person and that person—

9.1.a

holds the share in question, or

9.1.b

is part of a chain of persons—

9.1.b.i

each of which (other than the last) has a majority stake in the person
immediately below it in the chain, and

9.1.b.ii

the last of which holds the share.

9.2

A foreign power holds a right “indirectly” if the foreign power has a majority
stake in a person and that person—

9.2.a

holds that right, or

9.2.b

is part of a chain of persons—

9.2.b.i

each of which (other than the last) has a majority stake in the person
immediately below it in the chain, and

9.2.b.ii

the last of which holds that right.

9.3

For the purposes of sub-paragraphs  (1)  and  (2) , a foreign power has a
“majority stake” in a person if—

9.3.a

the foreign power holds a majority of the voting rights in the person,

9.3.b

the foreign power is a member of the person and has the right to appoint or
remove an officer of the person,

9.3.c

the foreign power is a member of the person and controls alone, or pursuant to
an agreement with other shareholders or members, a majority of the voting
rights in the person, or

9.3.d

the foreign power has the right to exercise, or actually exercises, dominant
influence or control over the person.

###### Shares held by nominees

10

A share held by a person as a nominee for another is to be treated as held by
the other (and not by the nominee).

###### Rights treated as held by person who controls their exercise

11

11.1

Where a person controls a right, the right is to be treated as held by that
person (and not by the person who in fact holds the right, unless that person
also controls it).

11.2

A person “controls” a right if, by virtue of any arrangement between that
person and others, the right is exercisable only—

11.2.a

by that person,

11.2.b

in accordance with that person’s directions or instructions, or

11.2.c

with that person’s consent or concurrence.

12

12.1

For the purposes of this Schedule, “ arrangement ” includes—

12.1.a

any scheme, agreement or understanding, whether or not it is legally
enforceable, and

12.1.b

any convention, custom or practice of any kind.

12.2

But something does not count as an arrangement unless there is at least some
degree of stability about it (whether by its nature or terms, the time it has
been in existence or otherwise).

###### Rights exercisable only in certain circumstances etc

13

13.1

Rights that are exercisable only in certain circumstances are to be taken into
account only—

13.1.a

where the circumstances have arisen, and for so long as they continue to
obtain, or

13.1.b

when the circumstances are within the control of the person having the rights.

13.2

But rights that are exercisable by an administrator or by creditors while a
person is in relevant insolvency proceedings are not to be taken into account
even while the person is in those proceedings.

13.3

“ Relevant insolvency proceedings ” means—

13.3.a

administration within the meaning of the Insolvency Act 1986,

13.3.b

administration within the meaning of the Insolvency (Northern Ireland) Order
1989 ( S.I. 1989/2405 (N.I. 19) ), or

13.3.c

proceedings under the insolvency law of another country or territory during
which a person’s assets and affairs are subject to the control or supervision
of a third party or creditor.

13.4

Rights that are normally exercisable but are temporarily incapable of exercise
are to continue to be taken into account.

###### Rights attached to shares held by way of security

14

Rights attached to shares held by way of security provided by a person are to
be treated for the purposes of this Schedule as held by that person—

14.a

where apart from the right to exercise them for the purpose of preserving the
value of the security, or of realising it, the rights are exercisable only in
accordance with that person’s instructions, and

14.b

where the shares are held in connection with the granting of loans as part of
normal business activities and apart from the right to exercise them for the
